Another Proof that Germany Denies Recognizing the Puppet Manchukuo

News from Tongji University

Yesterday, President Weng of Tongji University stated that regarding the rumors of Germany recognizing the puppet Manchukuo, they had repeatedly collected information from various German agencies. Reports from the school stated: "A telegram from the former German Maritime Society on February 26 stated, "The rumor that the Germans have recognized Manchukuo is absolutely denied and explicitly declared that all external and inaccurate news has no basis and is obviously a rumor created by traitors intending to harm Sino-German relations." Moreover, the German Minister also made a written statement stating that Germany has absolutely no intention of recognizing Manchukuo." The students of the former Japanese school originally planned to send a telegram advising the German government. However, because the German government has clearly explained this rumor, they have also stopped sending the telegram. In short, the relationship between China and Germany has always been good. From the perspective of the news obtained by German professors, the rumor is not worth believing.

The International Radio Station in Shanghai Held a Test Call with Fiji Yesterday

The International Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Communications purchased a Marconi wireless machine that can be used for both communication and telephone calls. The bureau has been testing calls with London, Berlin, San Francisco, Manila, and other places in recent days, preparing to officially launch wireless telephone service in the future. From 7 PM to 8 PM last night, it also tested a call with Manila. According to Xu Le, the engineer and business director of the International Radio Station, the results of testing calls with England, Germany, and the United States in recent days have been very good. The sound quality received during normal times is the same as that of a telephone in this city, and it is even better when the signal is clear. Currently, they are testing which wavelength is suitable for which time. Once the results are obtained, they will be reported for implementation. However, the testing is quite time-consuming, and it is currently difficult to predict when it will end. As for the current call records, they will not be released to the public for the time being. If there is an opportunity in the future, they will seek approval from Director Wen and invite members of the press for a test call.

Shanghai Banking Sector Regulates Rural Finance

Rural Loan Departments Established One After Another

Achievements of Shanghai Banks in One Year

Central News Agency reports: In recent years, domestic disasters have been frequent, causing cash to concentrate in urban areas, and the rural economy is gradually declining. The banking sector in Shanghai is aware of this, so it has recently engaged in regulating rural finance. For example, Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank and others have successively established rural loan departments and set up branches across the country. The achievements of the bank's rural loan department in the past year are recorded as follows:

Regulating Rural Finance is Related to the Whole Country

The main reason for the decline of the rural economy is the inability to regulate farmers' finance and the inability to sell agricultural products smoothly. The solution should be to transfer urban funds to the interior, so that rural finance can circulate. At the same time, improve the marketing system to ensure the smooth sale of agricultural products. If so, the farmers' economy will be prosperous, the purchasing power will increase, the market will prosper, and industry and commerce will develop accordingly. Therefore, regulating rural finance affects not only farmers, but the entire country. Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank and other banks in Shanghai are aware of the urgent need to regulate rural finance, so they have established rural loan departments and have set up branches in Nanjing, Zhengzhou, Changsha, and other places. They will gradually expand in the future.

Various Loans Released and Recovered as Scheduled

Although the bank's rural loan department was officially established in January last year, the amount of money coming in and out was very small in the first six months. The business gradually increased in August, and the amount of loans was also large. The loans issued include: 428,642 yuan for transportation and sales, 306,432 yuan for credit loans, and 287,521 yuan for warehouse loans, totaling 1,022,596 yuan. Except for the loans that have not yet reached the due date, all loans issued can be recovered as scheduled (many of them are repaid early).

Major Banks Extend Loans One After Another

As for the benefits obtained by the farmers in those areas, the most notable ones should be: (1) Rural finance can circulate. (2) When rural finance is tight, the interest rate for previous loans is very high, even as high as 3% to 4% per month. After the establishment of the loan department, farmers who borrow money are freed from the oppression of high interest rates. (3) Farmers often lack funds, making it difficult to start various businesses. After obtaining economic assistance, many businesses have been completed. Therefore, major banks in the city have decided to invest their real estate funds in rural finance and regulation across the country. When the farmers' economy becomes prosperous, the bank's own business will also flourish. It is heard that the Bank of Communications and the Zhejiang Industrial Bank are also planning to set up rural loan departments in various ports to enrich the farmers' economy.

Current Status of the Three Major Factories Under Preparation by the Ministry of Industry

Construction of the Ammonium Sulfate Factory Has Begun

Loan for the Paper Mill Approved by the Sino-British Board

Factory Site for the Machine Factory Located on Vacant Land in Wusong

The five major factories of steel, alcohol, paper, machinery, and ammonium sulfate, planned by the Ministry of Industry, have been prepared except for the steel and alcohol factories. The remaining three factories are now being actively pursued. The details learned are recorded as follows:

Construction of Ammonium Sulfate Factory Begins

The ammonium sulfate factory was to be jointly established with Brunner Mond & Co. of the United Kingdom, Brunner Mond & Co. of the State of Qu, and Aicci Co. of Germany, with a capital of 15 million yuan. However, the project was abandoned due to the harsh conditions proposed by the British and German sides. The Ministry of Industry believed that the various facilities of the factory were of great importance to the future of China's industry and national defense, so it decided to have it operated by Chinese people. The industrialist Fan Xudong contacted the Ministry of Industry to handle all the contracting procedures and decided to temporarily reduce the capital from 15 million yuan to 7 million yuan to facilitate the process. It is learned that Chen Gongbo, the Minister of Industry, submitted the detailed plan for establishing the factory to the 150th meeting of the Executive Yuan. The results of the discussion were that the exemption from taxes and fees and the reduction of transportation costs for maintaining the salt production part were approved after review. As for the issuance of 5.5 million yuan in public bonds, the Ministry of Industry was ordered to investigate the amount of shares already paid and the amount of debt owed by the factory before handling it according to law. It is also heard that after the plan of the factory was approved by the Executive Yuan, preparations were immediately carried out actively. The location of the factory was also selected at Jiadian, Pukou, Nanjing, and construction began the day before yesterday, with a deadline for completion and manufacturing within one year.

Loan for the Paper Mill Approved

The paper mill planned by the Ministry of Industry was originally intended to be jointly operated by the government and merchants, with a capital of 5 million yuan, of which 2 million yuan was from merchant shares, jointly subscribed by newspapers and bookstores. Xiaoxi in Qingtian County, Wenzhou, was also decided as the factory site. However, due to the decline in newspaper prices, merchants were concerned that the cost of raw materials would exceed the price of foreign paper, so they all took a wait-and-see attitude, and the project was halted. It is learned that the Ministry of Industry decided to run it solely by the government in order to implement its original intention, and submitted the entire plan of the factory to the Executive Yuan for approval. Regarding the funding for the establishment, it was decided to borrow 330,000 pounds from the Central Gengkuan (Boxer Indemnity) Commission for application. The loan has been approved by the Sino-British Board, and it is expected to be approved after review by the technical and financial committees. It is also learned that in order to expedite the process, the Ministry of Industry plans to organize a paper mill committee to plan everything in order to realize it as soon as possible.

Central Machine Factory Seeks Land in Shanghai

Since the Central Machine Factory was planned by the Ministry of Industry, it has been mostly completed and has contacted the Central Gengkuan (Boxer Indemnity) Commission to borrow 123,200 pounds for purchasing machinery. As for the factory site, it was previously decided to be in Caoxiexia, Xiaguan, Nanjing. However, because the terrain there is low-lying and cannot be used unless the soil is filled, the land price is limited after surveying and calculating, but the earthwork project is huge, costing more than 290,000 yuan. After much consideration, it was decided to move the factory to Shanghai, where industry is more developed, so that the products can be sold easily in the future. It is learned that the Ministry of Industry has selected a vacant land of about 50 acres in the southeast of Wusong Town. The land and water transportation there are very convenient. The evaluation and purchase procedures are currently underway, so that construction can begin in the near future.

Ministry of Communications, Navy, Finance, and General Staff Departments Hold Water Drawing Meeting Yesterday

Results of Discussion Difficult to Publish for the Time Being

Xin Sheng She reports that the right to draw water in our country has long been controlled by foreigners. Although negotiations have been made to recover the right and Chinese people have been successively appointed as pilots, foreign pilots have not been completely dismissed and are still being employed. The Ministry of Communications and other departments, in view of the intangible loss of sovereignty, specially convened a water drawing meeting at the Jianghai Customs yesterday afternoon. Xu Jixiang, the director of the Naval Administration Department of the Navy, Gao Tingzi, the director of the Shipping Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications, and representatives from the General Staff Department and the Ministry of Finance came to Shanghai to attend the meeting to discuss gradually reducing the number of foreign water drawing personnel and examining and employing Chinese people to take over, so as to actually achieve the complete recovery of the right. Gao Tingzi, the Director of the Shipping Administration Department, told the Xin Sheng She reporter that the results of yesterday's meeting were inconvenient to tell because they have not yet reached the stage of publication. The Shipping Administration Meeting of the Ministry of Communications is now scheduled to be held in Beijing on the 20th of this month. There are many proposals from all parties to reform the government, and they will be discussed item by item at the conference so that the domestic shipping industry can be refreshed.

The Wuhu-Zhejiang Railway Extends to Nanjing

Decision Made at Yesterday's Board of Directors Meeting

The Wuhu-Zhejiang Railway Company held a joint meeting of the board of directors and supervisors at around 4:00 yesterday afternoon. Many directors and supervisors attended, including Zhang Jingjiang, Li Shizeng, Ye Chucang, Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuesheng, Ye Zhuotang, and Zhang Danru. Zhang Xiaolin chaired the meeting, and it was decided that: (1) The Wuhu-Zhejiang railway line will be extended from Wuhu to Nanjing; (2) The annual shareholders' meeting will be held on the 12th of next month. It is heard that the railway construction is currently underway, the line has been built to Zhusigang, and it is already open to traffic.

The Two Railway Bureaus Improve Passenger Car Equipment

Special Emphasis on Third and Fourth Class Cars

The two railway bureaus, noting that the appearance and interior of the existing cars of all classes on the two lines have not yet been perfected, in addition to ordering the formulation of standard styles for the cars, instructed the Mechanical and Rolling Stock Departments to improve the following points in advance: (1) Those with old colors should be repainted to improve appearance. Although the color of each train cannot be absolutely uniform in terms of newness and depth, it should at least be similar. The principle of using domestic goods should be adopted for paint, and all tabletops for teacups in the carriages should be replaced with Chinese lacquer to avoid damage from heat; (2) The air in the carriages should be kept clean at all times, so there should be adequate ventilation equipment. Special attention should be paid to third and fourth class cars where passengers are crowded, and those without equipment should be installed as soon as possible; (3) In toilets of all classes of passenger cars, the lavatory equipment should be manufactured with porcelain; (4) The lighting in the carriages should be sufficient. The current lighting in third and fourth class cars is too dim and should be increased immediately; (5) The heating in the carriages in winter should be the same for third and fourth class cars as for first class cars; (6) Coat and hat hooks should be added to carriages where they are missing; (7) Third and fourth class cars have a large number of passengers, and fans should be installed in summer to emphasize hygiene; (8) The kitchen in the dining car should be equipped with electric ventilators to avoid odors from spreading. As the revenue from the two railways comes mainly from third and fourth class passenger tickets, special attention must be paid to the treatment of third and fourth class passengers. The two departments are instructed to discuss and handle this matter carefully and complete it within a time limit to benefit passengers.

The Municipal Council Stipulates the Maximum Rickshaw Rental Fee

Renting for 24 Hours

Costs 80 Cents

At the Municipal Council meeting held this Wednesday, a resolution was proposed to stipulate the maximum rickshaw rental fee at 80 cents for 24 hours of rental, with hourly reductions for rentals less than 24 hours, effective from July 1st. The rental fees for rickshaw companies will be determined by the Municipal Council, and a clause will be added to the rickshaw licenses stating that "rental fees shall not exceed the amount stipulated by the Municipal Council." The resolution was submitted to the Municipal Council by a joint committee composed of the Police Committee and the Transportation Committee. After much debate, it was decided that it would be discussed at the next meeting. The joint committee is currently continuing to study the report of the Rickshaw Committee.

The Cotton Industry Control Commission Dispatches Personnel to Shaanxi to Distribute Cotton Seeds

Cotton Seeds Detained in Lingbao Will Arrive in Xi'an Soon

Shanxi and Hunan Provinces Plan to Improve Cotton Seeds

The National Economic Council's Cotton Industry Control Commission, in response to the request of the Construction Department of the Shaanxi Provincial Government, jointly established the Cotton Industry Improvement Office with the province to improve cotton seeds in Shaanxi Province. The Cotton Industry Control Commission, recognizing that the national cotton production is insufficient to supply domestic yarn factories, resulting in foreign cotton invading our country's market and money flowing out, which is truly distressing, plans to make every effort to promote cotton planting in various provinces. The details are as follows:

Purchasing Improved Seeds: After the Shaanxi Provincial Government jointly established the Cotton Industry Improvement Office with the Cotton Industry Control Commission, it actively prepared to improve cotton seeds. Therefore, it entrusted the Cotton Industry Control Commission to purchase American cotton seeds in Zhangde, Henan, totaling 4,400 dan, which were transported to Lingbao by the Commission. Because the Shaanxi Provincial Government was troubled by economic difficulties, it negotiated with the Longhai Railway for free transportation to Tongguan. The railway has now approved the request, and the seeds will arrive at Tongguan soon. After arriving at Tongguan, they will be transported to Xi'an by long-distance bus.

Establishing Cooperatives: The Cotton Industry Control Commission, recognizing that the weather is gradually warming and cotton will be planted soon, specially dispatched Xu Zhongdi, an expert from the Raw Materials Department, to Shaanxi to establish the Cotton Industry Improvement Office to distribute cotton seeds. He departed the day before yesterday (the 7th) and will arrive on the 13th of this month. The above cotton seeds can be planted on more than 80,000 mu of cotton fields. Each mu can harvest about 50 sheng of cotton in a normal harvest, and the total annual harvest is about 400,000 dan, which can not only supplement the needs of national yarn factories but also reduce the import of foreign cotton. After farmers harvest and sell to the market, the Commission, fearing that merchants will manipulate prices, also plans to organize agricultural cooperatives so that farmers can get good prices when selling their produce.

Promoting in Various Provinces: After the Shaanxi Province cotton seed improvement, the Commission will also promote it in various provinces. Shanxi and Hunan are also in the planning stage. Because the soil in these two provinces contains saline, the irrigation method will be used first to gradually wash away the saline, and then cotton seeds will be planted to ensure that national cotton can be self-sufficient and does not need to rely on foreign cotton. However, it is still difficult to implement this in the short term. As for the investigation specialists sent to various places, because they need to conduct detailed investigations, it will be difficult for them to return to Shanghai in the near future.

The Central Mint Held a Review Meeting Yesterday

Reports by the Secretary and Assayer

The Review Committee of the Central Mint held its eleventh regular meeting at 4:30 yesterday afternoon in the grand auditorium on the third floor of the Central Bank on the Bund. The details are as follows:

Committee Members Present

The committee members present yesterday were Kong Xiangxi, Chen Xing, Xu Jiying, Lai Na, Ye Fuxiao, Lai Aisi, Dai Jinfu, Chen Guangfu, Xu Xinliu, Qin Runqing, Tai Wei, Hu Mengjia, Shi Demen, Hu Junzhuang, Wu Yunzhai, Ye Zhuo, Xi Demao, Shi Huang, etc. Those present were Lu Xuepu, Director of the Central Mint, Wei Jingzhou, Deputy Director, Qiao Furen, Secretary, etc., chaired by Kong Xiangxi.

Total Number of Coins Cast

The Secretariat reported on the newly minted coins and factory ingots, stating: "It was found that the mint minted new coins for 24 days in January of this year, totaling 4,531,584 yuan, with a daily average of 188,816 yuan. The number transferred to the Central Bank was 4,400,000 yuan, which is consistent with the number qualified by the Committee in January. In addition, 65 pieces of 999 factory ingots were produced in January, and 71 pieces (including 6 pieces in stock from December of last year) were transferred to the Central Bank. 2,730 pieces of 880 factory ingots were produced, and 2,600 pieces were transferred to the Central Bank. The number of A and B types of factory ingots produced above are consistent with those stamped by the Committee."

Assayer's Report

The Assay Department reported that the number of new coins minted by the Central Mint in February and sent for review by the Committee totaled 3.9 million yuan. 436 yuan have been extracted according to regulations for separate assaying. The average fineness is 880.31, which is 0.31 higher than the statutory standard. The weight is 26.6982 grams, which is about 0.0004 higher than the statutory weight, both within the statutory tolerance. Also, 3,458 pieces of 880 fineness B-type factory ingots qualified in the same month have been supervised by the assayer and stamped with the Committee's seal when calibrating the mark in accordance with regulations.

Hua Goods Exported to the U.S. Decreased Slightly in February

The Great American Evening News stated that according to the statistics released by the U.S. Consul General's Office in Shanghai, the total value of goods exported from Shanghai to the U.S. in February of this year was US$1,184,437, totaling US$2,374,728 including January. Among the goods exported in February, inedible animals and animal products still ranked first, with a total value of US$756,695, while in January it was US$766,117. The second was textiles, with a total value of US$384,390. The total for the two months was US$750,650. The third was plant foods and beverages, which decreased from US$32,757 in January to US$21,092 in February. Miscellaneous goods were US$4,890 in February, totaling US$5,264 for the two months. Metals and manufactured goods were US$4,107 in February. Non-metallic mineral products decreased from US$6,465 in January to US$5,679 in February. Chemicals and related items exported in February totaled US$3,627. Lumber and paper totaled US$2,259. The rest of the categories were all less than US$1,000. The goods exported from Shanghai to the Philippines in February decreased from US$136,171 in January to US$101,952. The goods exported to Hawaii in February also decreased from US$4,623 in January to US$2,401. Textiles ranked first among the goods exported to both places in February.

Tianjin Yuyuan Yarn Factory Scheduled to Resume Operations

A Total of 1,600 Workers Were Laid Off

The Xin Sheng News Agency stated that the Tianjin Yuyuan Yarn Factory, affected by the economic downturn, with accumulated yarn and financial difficulties, announced its shutdown at the end of last year. At a time when the party and government were addressing rural bankruptcy, the sudden increase in a large number of unemployed workers endangered social security. Therefore, they specially advised the capitalists to resume operations. The Shanghai Yarn Factory Federation received a telegram from Tianjin yesterday stating that the factory had complied with the mediation of the party and government, laid off 1,600 workers, and will resume operations as usual before the 15th of this month.

Public Concession Tram Workers Demand a General Wage Increase from the Company

Proposed Six Conditions for Adoption

Opposed the Unwarranted Dismissal of a Large Number of Workers

The Da Gong News Agency stated that the Shanghai Tram Company's Hart Road Old Factory and Tilanqiao New Factory employ a total of more than 2,000 drivers and conductors. The company's treatment of workers' wages is not generous. From February 1st of this year, the company increased workers' wages by 1.5 yuan, but the workers believed that the increase was too small and it was still difficult to maintain a livelihood, which inevitably led to malpractices. The company has successively dismissed as many as 40 conductors in the past month, which caused public outrage. They have reported to the union one after another, requesting negotiations.

Letter to the Company

The Three District Water and Electricity Workers' Union, after receiving reports from the workers, believed that the matter was of great importance. After several meetings, the result was that they would actively eliminate the bad habits of corruption. However, the treatment still needs to be improved. After public decision, a letter was sent to the Shanghai Tram Company, requesting adoption. The original letter said, "To the esteemed: According to reports from members of the union, the cost of living is high, and it is difficult to maintain a livelihood with the company's announced treatment of workers. Therefore, there are occasional malpractices by conductors, etc. Now, in order to be honest and clean on our own initiative, after several meetings, it has been decided that the problem of malpractices will be eliminated in the future. However, the problem of workers' treatment needs to be improved by the company. Six conditions for improvement have now been drafted, and it is proposed to negotiate with the company to maintain livelihoods and eliminate disputes, etc. Based on this, it is true that the income of workers serving the company does not cover expenses, and it is also true that ticket sellers, etc., engage in malpractices because they are forced to do so. Now, they are willing to reform themselves and demand improved treatment in order to obtain the double benefits of labor and management, which is only fitting. A special letter is sent to you, hoping that your company will adopt it and send a plenipotentiary representative to negotiate with the union's representatives on a regular basis to formally sign a treaty to eliminate all disputes and secure the livelihood of the workers, and we beg that you give a satisfactory reply within a week so that it can be forwarded to the workers."

Six Conditions

In order to maintain their livelihoods, the workers have put forward six conditions for improved treatment: (1) Starting from March 1934, the company should increase the workers' original wages by 8 yuan per month, and subsidize monthly housing expenses of 8 yuan; (2) All workers who are dismissed by the company or resign voluntarily will receive severance pay, one month's salary for those who have worked for one year, two months' salary for those who have worked for two years, and so on; (3) In the future, the company shall not accept reports from Chinese and foreign ticket inspectors without evidence; (4) Those who work for 22 days must apply for 4 days of work; (5) Workers who are sick and enter the hospital must be paid wages as usual; (6) The company shall not dismiss workers without reason.

Joint Meeting of Various Charitable Organizations Yesterday

The Process of Urgent Relief for the Yellow River Flood

The Shanghai Joint Association of Charitable Organizations for Fundraising for Urgent Relief for the Yellow River Flood held its sixth executive committee meeting at 4:00 yesterday afternoon at the Renji Hall on Yunnan Road. More than ten people attended, including Xu Shiying, Wang Yiting, Wang Xiaolai, Huang Hanzhi, Guan Jiongzhi, Zhu Ziqiao, Du Yuesheng, Qian Jingping, and Huang Bodu, chaired by Xu Shiying, with Ren Shizhen as the recorder. After the meeting began as usual, the chairman first reported on the statistics of receipts and disbursements of relief funds from the date of establishment to yesterday, as well as incoming and outgoing correspondence, and the progress of the work. He also ratified the allocation of 5,000 yuan and appointed Hong San and Zhang Zepu to go to Fuyang, Yingshang, and Taihe counties in northern Anhui to investigate and provide relief for bandit disasters, and the allocation of 1,000 yuan to provide relief for the flood disaster in more than 40 counties, including Gaolan, Gansu. Then, the discussion of various cases began: (1) Chairman Liu of Henan and others telegraphed that the flood in Hua County has suddenly risen four feet this time, the embankments have been completely destroyed, and countless people have been drowned and crushed to death by ice blocks. Tens of thousands of people who escaped have gathered in the county seat, leading and waiting to be fed, and there are wailings everywhere, and asked for swift relief. (2) The Yellow River Flood Relief Committee of Hebei Province sent a letter stating that the ice jam in Changyuan County had suddenly occurred, and the disaster victims had suffered a severe blow, and asked for a quick rescue. (3) The Changyuan County Flood Relief Committee telegraphed that the ice flood had suddenly occurred, and more than 100 villages on both sides of the embankment were devastated again. The old, young, women, and children climbed on the roofs and trees, and the sound of crying was extremely tragic. Personnel have been dispatched to rescue and accommodate them on the way. Please continue to allocate large amounts of money for relief. (4) The Shandong Poor People's Relief Association's Shanghai office for raising donations for Yellow River flood victims sent a letter stating that the Yellow River disaster victims are eating in the wind and sleeping in the dew, and are waiting to be fed, and it is urgent to carry out spring relief for rescue. (5) The party and government agencies of Yuanwu County, Henan, telegraphed jointly stating that the Yellow River flooded last year, the flat land was seven feet deep in water, and the horizontal flow did not stop for five days. Houses, livestock, fields, and crops were washed away. There are now 40,000 disaster victims who have no food or lodging and are in urgent need of relief. We beg you to quickly issue benevolence and come to the original area to distribute relief. (6) The Xinwei Relief Association sent a letter stating that it has approved the letter from the Shanghai Office of the Relief Committee, stating that the Fuzhou Branch of the Chinese Red Cross Relief Affairs telegraphed that the Fujian Rebellion has just been quelled, and the scars are all over the eyes. Please remember the unprecedented catastrophe and quickly allocate a large amount of money to rescue the survivors, and specially requested your association to appeal widely and raise a large amount of money to save the survivors. (7) Lawyer Yuan Xilian sent a letter stating that Yao Wu of Suzhou is willing to donate two boxes of fur clothes, valued at 3,000 yuan, to help with the relief, but the value must be the actual number of 3,000 yuan before they can be handed over. This year, the price of fur has fallen. If your association issues lottery tickets and uses this garment as a prize, then the three yuan can be sufficient. Please decide to handle the case. (Decision) Cases 1 to 5 will be provided after public fundraising. For Case 6, the Association will invite various groups to a meeting to jointly find ways to provide relief. In Case 7, no lottery tickets will be issued. Personnel will be sent to appraise the value, and it will be sold by colleagues. The meeting adjourned after discussion.

Opening of the Municipal Infectious Disease Hospital

The Municipal Bureau of Health has been actively preparing for the establishment of an infectious disease hospital due to the current lack of such facilities in the city. The Municipal Infectious Disease Hospital has been established on the former site of the Chinese Public Hospital on Tiantong'an Road in Zhabei and is now ready. Outpatient services will begin today. The details of the process are outlined below:

Preparatory Process: The Chinese Public Hospital in Zhabei was destroyed during the January 28th Incident. The Municipal Bureau of Health, recognizing the urgent need for an infectious disease hospital, repeatedly communicated with the hospital's board of directors. An agreement was reached to allocate the original site of the hospital to the Municipal Bureau of Health for the establishment of an infectious disease hospital. With the consent of the hospital authorities, the Municipal Bureau of Health immediately proceeded to formulate a plan, prepare a budget, and submit it to the municipal government for approval. Subsequently, Wu Liguo, the chief of the second section of the Municipal Bureau of Health, and others were appointed to begin preparations.

Opening Today: The Municipal Bureau of Health recognized that the existing buildings of the public hospital required renovation. The municipal government allocated funds for the renovation of the buildings and the purchase of essential medical supplies and equipment to meet the urgent need. Wu Liguo was officially appointed to temporarily serve as the director of the Municipal Infectious Disease Hospital, with Zhu Shenzhi as the chief of medical affairs and Ms. Xu as the chief of nursing. The hospital has fifty beds and will begin providing outpatient services today.

Future Plans: The Municipal Bureau of Health recognizes that the existing buildings of the hospital will not be sufficient to meet the needs of the city's large population in the future. The municipal government has approved an allocation of 30,000 yuan from the Zhabei Charitable Race Lottery to build two two-story Western-style buildings. Construction has already begun and is expected to be completed within six months. Plans are to expand the hospital to twenty-five buildings in the future, but the project has been temporarily postponed due to a lack of funding.

Shanghai Municipal Council to Increase Bicycle Tax

Effective from New Year's Day Next Year

Magnet Fee to be Increased Next Month

The municipal authorities of the French Concession recently informed the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement that the bicycle tax in the French Concession will increase from three yuan to four yuan per year starting January 1, 1935, and a magnet fee will be added. They inquired whether the Shanghai Municipal Council could do the same. This proposal was submitted to the Finance Committee on March 2nd and was deemed feasible. The issuance of bicycle licenses was initially intended for inspection and traffic management purposes, not primarily for tax revenue. However, considering the convenience enjoyed by cyclists and the cost of police management, increasing the tax to four yuan per year is not excessive. This proposal has now been approved by the board of directors and will be implemented next year. At the same time, starting April 1st of this year, a magnet fee will be added, estimated at about two jiao (cents) per piece. It is estimated that the increase in the bicycle tax will generate an additional 33,500 yuan in revenue per year.

Citizens from Various Roads Hold Meeting Yesterday Regarding False Rent Reduction Scheme

According to the Guowen News Agency, the Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Association held a joint meeting of representatives from various district branches yesterday afternoon at 2:00 pm to discuss the case of Wu Yongnian from Anhui, who is accused of collecting money under the false pretense of rent reduction. They sent a letter to the court requesting punishment. The details are as follows:

Representatives Present

Cai Qiaojun, Zheng Dongshan, Zhang Xianfang, Chen Jiufeng, Liu Zhongying, Ge Futian, Zhu Zhichun, Fang Peicheng, and more than ten other representatives from the 32nd, 38th, 29th, 27th, 26th, 15th, and 8th district branches of the First Special District Citizens' Association, elected Zhang Xianfang as chairman. Xu Zhaozhou, an official from the 32nd district branch, reported that Wu Yongnian from Anhui was collecting donations using unofficial receipts and forged seals of the 17th district branch in areas such as Qipu Road, which falls under the jurisdiction of the 32nd district. This action obstructs the rent reduction efforts. Although the case is being heard in court, it is requested that severe punishment be imposed. After the report,

Resolutions Passed

(A) Case of Wu Yongnian cleverly borrowing a name, illegally collecting donations, and forging seals, exceeding his authority: (Resolved) (1) Send a letter to the court requesting severe punishment; (2) Dispatch Xu Zhaozhou, an official from the 32nd district branch, to testify regarding the illegal actions. (B) Efforts to reduce rent: (Resolved) (1) District branches fill out forms and submit them to the association; (2) Establish rent reduction branches in their respective areas; (3) For rent reduction procedures that have been completed, such as Jiangxi Road and more than ten other roads; (4) Solicit shops and residents in their respective areas to join the association as members to strengthen unity; (5) The association will protect the welfare of citizens and will accept and handle matters other than rent reduction.

Letter to the Court

To: Shanghai First Special District Court,

We hereby report that Wu Yongnian from Anhui has forged the seal of the 17th district branch and illegally collected fees in the Qipu Road area, which falls under the jurisdiction of the 32nd district branch of our association. The case is currently being heard by your esteemed court, and the 32nd district branch has dispatched official Xu Zhaozhou to testify to the court. The joint meeting of representatives of our association has resolved that this matter concerns the reputation of the association and obstructs the progress of our work. Such illegal actions should be severely punished as a warning to others. Accordingly, we submit this case to your esteemed court, requesting that you investigate and punish the illegal act according to the law, for the sake of public convenience. Sincerely, The Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Association.

X-Ray Expert Shen Chengwu Opens Practice

Shen Chengwu is the great-grandson of the late Marquis Wen Su of Minhou and the seventh son of Mr. Ai Cang. In 1920, he went to Europe to study medicine at Tongji University, first at the University of Berlin and then at the University of Vienna in Austria. After passing the national examination, he obtained a doctorate in medicine. Afterwards, he stayed in Germany and Austria to practice various specialties. Later, he specialized in X-ray science for five years. After thirteen years abroad, he has now brought the latest X-ray equipment to establish a research institute at No. 882 Jing'an Temple Road, across from the Zhangjia Garden, specializing in X-ray deep and superficial therapy and various diagnoses.

Silverware Industry Workers on Hunger Strike for Five Days

Chinese Red Cross Society Seeks Relief

Last year, workers from the Sanyou Industrial Society were stranded in Shanghai. The Chinese Red Cross Society provided rice for relief, and after the labor unrest was resolved, the workers presented the Red Cross Society with a plaque expressing their gratitude. The society has now received a letter from the Shanghai Silversmiths' Union stating that Chen Yongchang and seventeen others have been on a hunger strike for four days at the Silversmiths' Guildhall on Huayuan Street outside the Datongmen. They request relief. Wang Peiyuan, the director of the society, immediately notified Dr. Lü Shoubai of the 16th Pu Third Hospital to provide relief quickly to prevent accidents.

Changsha Shallow Water Fees Reduced Today

Originally Increased by 50%

Now Changed to 20%

The water level in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River was very shallow last time, making navigation difficult. The six shipping companies in Shanghai had increased the shallow water surcharge by 50% on the Hankou-Changsha section. Recently, the river water in the upper reaches has risen, and navigation on the Hunan route is now free. Yesterday, after a meeting of the six companies, it was decided that from today, the freight rate for the Hankou-Changsha section will be reduced by 30% from the previous 50% increase, changing it to a shallow water surcharge of 20%. This has been notified to all customs brokers and passengers.

National Cargo Transportation to Change to Kilogram System Starting June 1st

100 Jin Equals 60.479 Kilograms

Various Shipping Companies Busy Preparing

The import and export of goods in Shanghai have always been calculated in terms of dan (picul), tonnage, and size. For example, one ton of goods is calculated as 2,240 pounds in weight or 40 cubic feet in size. If calculated in dan, it is customary to use 100 pieces as one dan. The shipping companies' import and export cargo transportation charges are also calculated based on this weight. For decades, although freight rates have fluctuated, the weights and measures have always been based on this method. Recently, the Ministry of Finance implemented the new weights and measures system and has decided that from June 1st of this year, the national customs will uniformly use kilograms to calculate import and export goods. After receiving this order, the shipping companies in Shanghai realized that the original freight charges and calculation methods based on weight would have to be completely overturned. The freight rates must be revised according to the new regulations. As the date of implementation is not far away,

The various companies are currently revising the freight rates. The information gathered is recorded below:

Changes to Dan

Regardless of whether goods are imported or exported from the Yangtze River, inland rivers, or coastal areas, the payment of tax rates and freight charges is generally based on three categories: valuation, weight, and size. Most of the grains, salt, sugar, and northbound and southbound shipments are calculated by weight, so the freight charges in the shipping companies' tariff are more frequently based on weight than on size. Historically, the weight of goods has been based on the dan. Sixteen dan and eighty jin equal one ton, and freight charges are determined accordingly. Now, the new regulations of the Ministry of Finance abolish the originally established system of 100 jin per dan and convert all weight-based goods to kilograms. The specified amount of 100 jin is equivalent to 60.479 kilograms. That is, 100 jin of goods is converted to 60.479 kilograms, and one ton is equivalent to 1059 dan and a bit more. This is different from the original 168 dan.

Revision of Freight Charges

Because weight-based goods must be converted to kilograms, the weighing of goods that go on and off ships will be done using kilogram scales that the shipping companies and cargo warehouses will uniformly obtain from the Ministry of Finance. The packaging of various goods will also use kilograms as the unit. The originally set freight charges for various Yangtze River and sea routes will be revised for weight-based goods converted to kilograms, while a small number of goods based on size and valuation will not need to be changed. The shipping companies in Shanghai are already discussing the new kilogram freight rates. For example, the freight rate for goods going up the Yangtze River to Hankou, which was originally 9 jiao (cents) per dan, will increase to 1 yuan and 4 jiao and 9 fen after the conversion to kilograms. The original price of 1 yuan and 6 jiao will increase to 2 yuan and 6 jiao and 4 fen, and the original price of 2 yuan and 4 jiao will increase to 3 yuan and 9 jiao and 6 fen, an increase of 65% over the original freight rate. This is not only the case for the Yangtze River, but also for the coastal areas.

Implementation on June 1st

The new kilogram system has been identified by the Jianghai Customs and will be implemented from June 1st of this year. The area of implementation includes not only the Yangtze River, the North and South Seas, and various inland rivers, but also all areas under the jurisdiction of the central government. Before May 31st, all shipping companies must complete the revision of the new freight rates for various routes, print and distribute new tariff booklets to customs brokers and passengers. Goods shipped from foreign ports to Shanghai will also be handled in the same way. The shipping companies have already notified their branch offices in various locations to quickly prepare for the conversion to kilogram freight rates and to expedite all procedures related to this matter in order to avoid being caught off guard and hindering the implementation of government orders. It is said that the most important aspect of the central government's conversion to the kilogram system is the increase in salt tax revenue. It is estimated that after the rigorous implementation of the new system, annual salt tax revenue can increase by 30% to 40%. Currently, salt merchants in various regions are requesting an exemption from the conversion.

Love Suicide Case at the Yangtze Hotel

Not Due to Economic Reasons

But Due to Unfree Marriage

At around 4:00 PM the day before yesterday, a young man and a woman resembling a female student checked into the Yangtze Hotel on Hankou Road. The front desk led them to Room 724 on the seventh floor. The young man identified himself as Ge Yiqun, a 24-year-old from Pinghu. He stated that the woman was his relative. He paid seven yuan for the room and the staff delivered tea and water to the room. The young man then made three or four phone calls to friends in Nanshi. Soon after, several guests visited, but left shortly after. Around 8:00 PM, the two had dinner in the room and did not go out. Around 9:00 PM, they closed the door and went to bed. However, at 12:00 PM yesterday, the two had not yet gotten up. A tea server at the hotel went to knock on the door to ask if the room was still needed, as is customary. However, there was no response for a long time, so he became suspicious. He found a way to open the door and enter, and found the two lying side by side in bed, their faces pale, their necks wrapped with a trouser belt, white foam coming from their mouths, and they had been dead for a long time. The tea server was shocked and immediately reported it to the front desk, who in turn reported it to the Laozha Police Station. Patrol officer No. 106 rushed to the scene to investigate. He searched the room and found two suicide notes, which stated that they were not dying for economic reasons, but because their marriage was not free. The patrol officer transported the two bodies to the Forensic Examination Office on Fielun Road, pending an examination by the court this morning. He reported back to the police chief and filed the suicide notes for investigation to determine the identities of the deceased and the truth before proceeding.

Murder Due to Failed Loan Request

Tang Zhaokun Dies Tragically

Tang Zhaokun, a 33-year-old resident of foreign origin residing at No. 247 in the Yangjiadu garbage pond in Pudong, owned two barges and was a small businessman. A fellow villager, Hou Zhenqing, recently asked him for a loan of several yuan, but Tang refused, saying he had no money. Hou left disappointed. At around 12:00 PM yesterday, Hou suddenly arrived again. Tang offered him a meal and ordered his wife to go ashore to buy cigarettes. While she was gone, Hou took the opportunity to ask Tang for a loan. When they disagreed, Hou pulled out a gun and fired a shot at him, hitting him in the head. He fell to the ground, covered in blood. The murderer took the opportunity to escape without a trace. When Zhaokun's wife returned, she immediately reported it to the water patrol team, who took him to Baolong Hospital, but he died at 6:10 PM.

Wife Inraged, Dies of Poisoning

Trouble Often Starts From Small Things

According to Wang Jiazhu, he had called the female servant to eat, and his wife said, "What does it have to do with you whether she eats or not?" and then argued with him. After obtaining this information, Mr. Guo ruled that the deceased Wang Tangshi had indeed died from opium poisoning and handed the body over to her husband, Wang Jiazhu, with a signed statement for him to take back for coffin burial.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to Implement Anti-Theft Equipment on All Ships

Puan Wheel Has Been Installed and Scheduled to Sail to Qingdao Today

Kidnapped Passengers Still Have No News of Escape

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Shanghai-Qingdao line Puan Wheel has been repaired and equipped with anti-theft equipment. It is scheduled to sail to Qingdao this morning. The kidnapped passengers have not yet escaped. The details are as follows:

Repaired and Reopened

After the Puan Wheel collided with a British blue funnel cargo ship on the Huangpu River, it was taken to the Gaochangmiao Naval Jiangnan Shipyard for repairs. It has now been repaired and all the cabins and seats have been repainted. It is scheduled to sail from Shanghai to Qingdao at 9:00 AM this morning, resuming its schedule. It was berthed at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Huazhan in Pudong yesterday. As for the British blue funnel company's request for compensation for losses, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company believes that it was not at fault, so the issue of liability for the collision will be decided according to law.

Anti-Theft Device Installation

After the Executive Yuan issued the anti-theft regulations, Liu Hongsheng, the general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, decided to install anti-theft equipment on all river and sea ships in accordance with the law. The Puan Wheel on the Shanghai-Qingdao line was the first to be equipped. It has now been installed. Iron doors have been installed to separate the first-class cabins, second-class cabins, and steerage. The bridge deck has also been equipped with iron doors to prevent unauthorized personnel from entering. All first-class passengers must have a guarantor when purchasing tickets for prevention. The above measures will be implemented from today.

Rescuing Passengers

The Puan Wheel was hijacked by pirates in Dapeng Bay outside Wusongkou while sailing from Shanghai to Qingdao. Regarding the case of nine passengers being kidnapped, the families of the passengers sent representatives to Shantou to negotiate with the pirates regarding ransom payments. However, because the pirates demanded too much money, there has been no news of escape for two months. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company needs to have Sun Zhenwu, the manager of the Qingdao branch, return to Shanghai to preside over the joint transportation with the Jiaoji Railway. A telegram has been sent to Sun Zhenwu urging him to return to Qingdao from Guangdong as soon as possible so that it can be implemented soon.

In the First Criminal Court's trial, the police prosecuted Mao Renfu for repeated theft. Mao Renfu confessed to the theft without denial. The court ordered the defendant to be remanded to custody and scheduled sentencing for the 14th.

The Case of the Woman Hanging Herself in Chongming, Opening the Coffin

Decomposed Flesh Makes Confirmation Difficult

Unknown Use for Foreign Potatoes

Qiu Chuanlang, a villager from Xinkaihe Town in Chongming, had a daughter named Yin Xian, who was married to Yang Miaolang, a farmer in the same area. They had separated due to disagreements, but later reconciled after litigation. In May of the previous year, according to the old lunar calendar, Yin Xian suddenly hanged herself in the living room of their home. Qiu Chuanlang then filed a lawsuit accusing Yang Miaolang of causing her death through harm. The case remained unresolved in the original county, so the High Court instructed the Shanghai Local Court to transport the coffin to Shanghai for re-examination at the Zhenru Forensic Institute. The institute has now opened the coffin, revealing that the deceased's flesh has decomposed. There were foreign potatoes in the coffin, the purpose of which is unknown. The deceased's abdomen contained a fetus with a human form. However, due to the decomposition of the body, the presence of skin or injuries on it cannot be confirmed. Therefore, a preliminary examination was conducted, and it was reported that the ribs under the breasts seemed to show signs of injury, but it was stated that this could not be confirmed. The institute will remove all the bones and decomposed flesh, use chemicals for testing, and then provide a report to the court. Director Lin of the institute also questioned both parties about the circumstances at the time for reference. According to Qiu Chuanlang, after his daughter's marriage, she was manipulated by her husband's younger sister, leading to mistreatment by her mother-in-law. Her husband, listening to his mother and sister, formed a group of abusers and inflicted beatings, which was the reason for the litigation over separation. He also stated that the so-called hanging occurred at noon, but farmers typically return home for lunch at noon, so it would be impossible for anyone to witness the suicide. Therefore, he alleged that it was a premeditated murder followed by a hanging to create a misleading situation. The defendant, Yang Miaolang, still claimed that his wife committed suicide because she was scolded for not being able to find clothes at her parents' home and became angry. Director Lin then dismissed them and told them to await further instructions.

Captain Lu immediately dispatched detectives Pan Huanzhang and others, all disguised as workers, to the teahouse to wait. Soon, two men entered, looked around, and then began whispering to each other. The detectives deemed their actions suspicious and gave a prearranged signal. They drew their weapons and ordered the men to stand up and be searched. A Browning pistol and two bullets were found on Zhang Jinfu. An eight-inch revolver and three bullets were found on Zhu Koukou. At the same time, another accomplice, Jiang A'gen, was apprehended at the entrance of the teahouse. After they were brought back to the team, Captain Lu conducted a preliminary interrogation. Zhang Jinfu, 31 years old from Nantong, confessed that at 7:00 PM on September 20th of last year, he and five other acquaintances, including Lu Jintao, robbed the Dingfeng Candle and Soap Factory at Xinqiao Tou, Old West Gate, stealing 1,300 yuan in banknotes and 3,000 jiao in small change. They took the money to a small inn on East Zilaihuo Street in the French Concession, where they divided the loot and spent it. Three pistols were used during the robbery, two of which are the ones he carried today. There was also a six-inch Browning pistol that Lu Jintao had. However, Lu Jintao has been arrested by the Xinzha Police Station, and the weapon has been confiscated. He also confessed that around June of last year, he, Zhou Zilian, A'si, and others carried two pistols and robbed a tobacco and paper shop on Jumen Road, stealing over 40 yuan, which they divided and spent. Recently, A'er, who had been a steward at the Tonghe Sauce Garden near the Small West Gate, was dismissed by the owner and harbored resentment. He proposed robbing the garden. After discussing it with Zhou Zilian and A'si, Zhou Zilian instructed him to recruit Zhu Koukou and Jiang A'gen. Zhou Zilian then distributed two pistols to Zhang Jinfu and Zhu Koukou, and they agreed to go to the Tonghe Sauce Garden to rob it tonight. However, because it was still early, they were drinking tea at the Sunji Teahouse while waiting for the right opportunity when they were caught. Zhou Zilian and A'si managed to escape. Zhu Koukou (aka Lao Er, 32 years old, residing at 59 Tangjia Bay) and Jiang A'gen (aka Ma Shun, 40 years old, residing at 5 Kangti Road) confessed that Zhou Zilian asked them to go to the robbery with Zhang Jinfu and others to secretly monitor their actions and prevent them from escaping with the stolen goods. Because the matter concerned a robbery case, Captain Lu ordered a written report to be prepared and the three robbers, along with the weapons, to be sent to the Third Division of the General Bureau for interrogation and punishment.

Russian Dies in Detention Center

Russian citizen Shidelainigefu Alaige Shangte (transliteration), 40 years old, was homeless and begging for a living in Shanghai. At 4:30 PM on the 8th, he was found drunk and unconscious at the corner of Songshan Road and Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession. A French police officer from the French Police Station found him while patrolling and brought him to the Xiahfei Road Police Station, then sent him to the Lujiawan General Police Station for detention. At 8:45 PM that evening, he died in the detention center. The guard discovered the body and reported it to the head of the police station, who sent detectives to transport the body to the autopsy room of the Shanghai Municipal Council Hospital on Tairas Tuol Road. Yesterday morning, the Second Special District Local Court appointed Prosecutor Wang Ren and a forensic doctor to examine the body, confirming that the deceased died of illness. The body was buried by the Western Charities Association of the Shanghai Municipal Council.

Suspicious Cause of Death of Unknown Male Corpse

At around 8:30 AM on the morning of the [day of the week not specified], a doctor from the Southeast Medical College of Zhenru, on his way from Shanghai to the college, was traveling by car along the Beizhongshan Road near the Shanghai West Power Plant when he suddenly saw a man resembling a worker lying on the ground, with three or four villagers looking on. The doctor stopped the car and examined the man closely, finding that he was severely injured and on the verge of death. He inquired with the villagers, who said that they had just seen an empty truck carrying lime, with six or seven workers lying on the truck bed, speeding from north to south. When it reached that spot, the man suddenly fell off, and the truck continued speeding away. It was assumed that the other workers and the driver on the truck had not noticed. The doctor immediately helped the man into the car and took him to the hospital, but he had already died. The hospital reported the incident to the Fourth District Third Precinct, which then reported it to the Sixth District because the incident occurred within the Sixth District's jurisdiction. After receiving the report, District Chief Tan ordered Police Chief Hu to first investigate the scene of the incident and inquire with the villagers, but they only said that they saw the man fall from an empty truck, and because it was driving so fast, they could not see the license plate. The unnamed man was about 30 years old, and his clothes were old and worn. He died from internal injuries and brain trauma. A photograph and fingerprints were taken, and the area was reported to the Local Court for examination. District Chief Tan ordered an investigation into the truck and the man's family so that the case could be investigated.

Fine for Private Sale of Tax-Evasion Cigarettes

Fengtai Yin Paper Shop at 253 Rue de la Republique, French Concession, and Zhifeng Tobacco and Paper Shop at 235 Route Tenant de la Tour, have recently been privately selling tax-evading cigarettes. Wu Yao'a, a Western detective, and Zhou Baosheng and Zhu Qiming, Chinese detectives from the French Concession Cigarette Investigation Office of the Ministry of Finance's Consolidated Tax Bureau, found out about it. On the morning of the day of the week not specified, they went to Fengtai Shop and confiscated 955 cigars, and to Zhifeng Shop and confiscated 504 cigars. Yesterday, the manager of Fengtai [name missing] and Chen Songshi, the accountant of Zhifeng, were summoned to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court. Fei Xizhen, the police lawyer, presented the case, charging them with violating Article 217, Paragraph 7 of the Rules for Inspection and Punishment of the Ministry of Finance's Tobacco Consolidated Tax Bureau, and the tax evasion regulations. After questioning the defendants, Judge Sun Pengzhen determined that the cigarettes were brought in by street vendors, and they did not know they were tax-evading and illegal. The court immediately sentenced Chen Yi to a fine of 40 yuan and Chen Songshi to a fine of 30 yuan. The tax-evading cigarettes were confiscated.

Robbery at Wangjiaqiao in the Second District of the County

At around 2:00 AM the other night, several bandits suddenly broke into the home of Huang Qingyu in Wangjiaqiao Village, Second District of the county. They were all wearing uniforms, carrying long guns, and speaking in a Hakka accent. They broke into the house through the eastern corner gate of the Huang residence. The owner's family awoke and immediately put on clothes, went outside and rang a gong to alert the neighbors. Villagers gathered in response to the alarm, surrounding the house to arrest the bandits. Yang Guozhen, the head of the sixth jia of the district's defense corps, also arrived with his corps members while patrolling. The bandits were caught off guard and fled in all directions. However, due to the darkness of the night, two of the bandits were unfamiliar with the roads and were apprehended, along with two long guns and over one hundred bullets. They were immediately handed over to the corps headquarters. They identified themselves as Sun Tingzhen and Hu Deyi, both from Henan. Yesterday, the corps prepared a document and sent the two bandits, along with the guns and ammunition, to the county government for interrogation.

We have found that today (i.e., March 9), your newspaper's local news column contains information that a British employee of the Health Department of the British Works Bureau, Mr. Hoffer, sent a letter to 475 Lafayette Road, Weiltai, by post last month, containing a HSBC bank check. However, because the letter was mistakenly delivered by the postman to 275 Lafayette Road, the check was fraudulently claimed by others. The information in the newspaper is unfounded," etc. In addition to obtaining a statement from the sender for filing with the bureau, we hereby inform you and hope that you will correct it as soon as possible to conform to the facts. Sincerely, To the Shen Bao Newspaper Office, Shanghai Postal Administration, March 9.

Reading Q&A

Regarding Literature Learning Steps, Writing and Other Matters

丨General Answer to Messrs. Wang Qilun, Chen Ziyuan, Guo Jingwu, Jin XX, etc.

Recently, we have received many letters inquiring about the learning steps of literature, writing and other scattered questions that are of concern to beginners who are very enthusiastic about literature. The senders are either workers or shop assistants, and they are all young. According to their letters, two or three of them have attended junior high school, but dropped out due to family financial difficulties. The situation of the rest is even worse, they have only received elementary school education. Forced by poverty, they cannot obtain the educational opportunities they deserve, so they run out of school to participate in social production. The busyness of work, even if they want to attend night school for remedial studies, is not allowed by time and circumstances. However, relying on their self-study efforts, judging from their letters, the fluency and clarity of their writing is not necessarily inferior to that of ordinary college students, or even better. This makes us ashamed, enough to break the general discrimination against the cultural ability of the masses; but at the same time, it also makes us realize the important significance of our work: to improve the cultural level of the masses, and to cultivate and promote writers who are truly their own from their midst. This work is not only possible, but also necessary.

They doubt their own abilities, they hover, groping for the way forward. We have said several times that ability can be improved through self-study, and it is not necessary to enter school to cultivate it. At the same time, we have also cited many famous figures in literary history as examples. In fact, why do we need to look far for examples? Just look back at your own progress in self-study, can't you go forward bravely? The achievements of each stage are waiting for you.

We are not literary scholars, we are also groping for the way forward just like you. However, in this process, perhaps our knowledge is a little more than yours, and a little clearer. Regarding the inquiries, we hereby humbly offer our opinion for your consideration.

Let's first discuss the learning steps. Mr. Wang's proposed plan is divided into three stages: the first stage, "read more works of literary value on the one hand, and practice writing more on the other hand; "the second stage: when" the first stage "has a considerable foundation, then start studying Chinese literature"; the third stage is to study Western literature. Mr. Guo's proposed plan is: to obtain a systematic understanding of literary theory as the first stage, to seek a deeper exploration of literary theory, and to study creative methods and works as the second stage; to continue the theoretical and work studies and begin the study of social sciences as the third stage. Here, Mr. Guo also made an accompanying statement that his original intention was only to study literature, and he would only read social science books if possible. This view is the same as that of another reader, Mr. Pan. He has read many literary books and wants to devote himself to literature, but now he also wants to read some social science books, fearing that he will not succeed in both if he is distracted.

We feel that there are many shortcomings in the learning steps proposed by Mr. Wang and Mr. Guo, both in principle and in practical application. First, both gentlemen, especially Mr. Wang, completely ignore the necessity of understanding social sciences for the appreciation, research and creation of literature. We know that literature is a department of art, and art is a reflection of the times and society, and implies the author's understanding and hope for the times and society in which they are located, expressed in concrete images. In this way, without a correct understanding of social sciences such as economics, political science, sociology, psychology?…etc. as the foundation, it is simply impossible to obtain a complete understanding of the appreciation and research of literature. If we do not have social sciences to help us fight for social understanding, then our creation will become empty in content and become a hodgepodge and game of literature. It is true that in the past, and even today, there are many hodgepodges and games of words that are popular without any so-called content, playing their "helpful idler" role. But these are just foam on the surface of the water, and will be swept away by the torrent of the times without a trace. We busy people should not follow those decadent idlers to play with literature by selling air and buying air. We should use literature as our horn to call out our wishes for society, and also to awaken busy people like us. Only by doing this can we be true to the meaning of being a literary scholar, and only by doing this will we not be left behind. To do this, we can say that our idea of ​​being a literary scholar is noble. Therefore, studying social sciences is a necessary condition, and it cannot be said to be a distraction. Only by working hand in hand with social sciences can we expect considerable achievements in literary research and creation. Second, Mr. Wang's first step of the plan is to read more works of literary value on the one hand and practice writing more on the other hand, which is impeccable and better than Mr. Guo's starting with the exploration of literary theory, because literary theory involves general works to some extent. If you have not read some works first, you will not have a deep understanding of literary theory; what's more, literary theory is based on the methods of social sciences, but Mr. Guo puts the research of social sciences on the butt of the last stage. But Mr. Wang's so-called first stage, we feel, is necessary for every stage. Works are coming to your face inexhaustibly; and articles are not a limited period of time, and can reach the realm of perfection. In fact, articles never reach the realm of perfection. Third, Mr. Wang's so-called second stage starts to study Chinese literature, and the third stage studies Western literature, which probably refers to the exploration of history. Otherwise, just flipping through the works is simply driving the second and third stages into the scope of the first stage. But the study of literary history must have a deep foundation, and cannot ignore the exploration of general theory. Mr. Wang's plan is too broad and too empty, and it is not easy to start with. The result will still fall into a state of random collision. In this regard, Mr. Guo's plan is actually better than Mr. Wang's, and more in line with practical application. (To be continued)

Liu Changchun Left Beiping for Shanghai Yesterday

Beiping to Hold Basketball Pre-selection Starting on the 13th

(Beiping Special Dispatch) The Far Eastern Games are scheduled to be held in Manila in mid-May. Five countries including China, Japan, the Philippines, the Dutch East Indies, and Annam will participate. The Sports Promotion Association will hold a board meeting in Shanghai on the 10th. Wang Zhengting went south today (the 8th), and the Northeast strongman Liu Changchun is also scheduled to go to Shanghai tomorrow (the 9th). The Beiping City Basketball Team is also preparing to participate in the Far Eastern Games. The situation in each area is recorded as follows,

Wang Zhengting Talks

Wang Zhengting, a director of the National Sports Promotion Association, took the Pingpu Express to Beijing and then to Shanghai at 5:35 pm today (the 8th). The reporter met with Wang at the station. According to Wang, he originally planned to come to Ping after the Sports Promotion Association meeting, but due to busy work, he came to Ping in advance. This trip to participate in the Sports Promotion Association is to discuss various issues related to China's participation in the Far Eastern Games. Among them, the method of pre-selection for Chinese athletes to participate in the Far Eastern Games, the hiring of instructors, and the funding issue are particularly important. He will accompany the athletes to the Philippines in early May. Although sports in China have made progress in recent years, there are still few opportunities to compete internationally. This participation in the Far Eastern Games is one of the international competitions. He hopes that the athletes will work hard and win glory for the motherland. China College is conducting fundraising to investigate the addresses of graduate students and plans fundraising methods. The College of Science is planning to expand. He will purchase British, German, and French instruments in Shanghai to meet the needs. As for the decision of the China College basketball team to go to Shanghai to have friendly matches with various universities in Shanghai, he donated 200 yuan for travel expenses, and the shortfall will be supplemented by the college.

Liu Changchun Speaks

Northeast track and field athlete Liu Changchun will travel to Shanghai via the through train on the Pingpu line at 8:30 AM on the 9th to train in Shanghai and prepare to participate in the upcoming Games. This reporter interviewed Mr. Liu, who stated that his trip to Shanghai for training is to prepare for participating in the Far Eastern Games. He will exert his full effort and strive forward. The expenses for this training in Shanghai are borne entirely by himself, and he will not seek assistance from anyone. He is scheduled to leave for Tianjin and then Shanghai at 8:30 AM tomorrow (the 9th). Whether he will participate in the North China Games after the Far Eastern Games will be decided after returning to Peiping, he said. It is heard that the Northeast football team is scheduled to make a long journey to Shanghai, Nanjing, and Hankou at the end of this month or the end of the month, for a period of one month. Liu Changchun has been invited to Shanghai to make arrangements.

Professors, instructors, and athletes from Peiping and the Northeast are actively opposing the puppet Manchurian state's request to participate in the Far Eastern Games. Public Education Center Holds Shuttlecock Kicking Competition

Scheduled to be Held on March 18th

Registration Begins Immediately

The Shanghai Municipal Public Education Center recently held a shuttlecock kicking competition, scheduled to be held on March 18th. Registration begins immediately. The methods are as follows: (1) This center, in order to promote national skills and attach importance to shuttlecock kicking, aiming to improve physical training, is holding a shuttlecock kicking competition; (2) All citizens with shuttlecock kicking skills, regardless of gender or age, may register to join the competition; (3) The competition date is set for March 18th; (4) The quota is 40 people; (5) The competition venue is the lecture hall of this center; (6) During the competition, it will be divided into adult and children's groups. Children are from 8 to 15 years old, and adults are 16 years old and above; (7) Competition rules (A) If someone arrives late when the roll is called, they must wait until the entire competition is over before they can join in. Those who do not arrive will be considered to have given up; (B) No actions that interfere with the competitors are allowed; (C) No loud shouting is allowed; (D) Compete according to the number. No jumping the gun is allowed; (E) If the competition is illegal or irregular, the judges may sound a whistle to stop it; (F) If someone does not listen to the instructions of the judges, they may be ordered to leave; (G) No substitutions are allowed during the competition; (H) The shuttlecock kicking competition is temporarily limited to three types: designated kicking, circling kicking, and performance. The competitors must obey; (8) The competition equipment will be prepared by this center; (9) The judges will be hired by this center; (10) The awards will be divided into adult and children's categories. The top three will be selected based on the average score. The prizes will be given by this center separately; (11) Registration date: from now until the 15th of this month; (12) Registration location: Office of this center.

Ministry of Education Introduces League of Nations Educational Films

The Chinese Educational Film Association purchased 30 sets of educational films from the Italian International Educational Film Association. They were transferred to the Ministry of Education's Department of Social Affairs, which yesterday sent a circular to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities, as well as public and private universities, to rent them according to the rental method. The films are related to physics, chemistry, biology, medicine, astronomy, etc., and the content is quite wonderful. The names of the films and the rental methods are listed below:

List of League of Nations Educational Film Names

Historical Rome, Eye Surgery, Tree Oil, Making Brass Wire, Guruji Lamp, Jump, Common Lung Disease Patients, Streaming Gas, Steel, Religious Festival, Chicken Changes from Egg, Life of Bees, Wood Nan Luo Glass Manufacturing, Flies, Plant Life, Living Crystals, Sea Garden, Planetary System, Crystalline Phenomena, German Capital in the 19th Century, Carrara Marble Production, Silver Han Wonders Soap Bubbles, Sri Lanka Peak,

Methods for Renting League of Nations Educational Films

(1) Educational institutions or schools that rent League of Nations educational films must contact the Nanjing General Association of the Chinese Educational Film Association (temporarily attached to the Ministry of Education); (2) Educational institutions or schools that rent the aforementioned films must be responsible for care and custody; (3) The aforementioned 30 sets of films are divided into six groups. Each group is shown for one day and the rent is 15 yuan. The total rent for all the performances is 90 yuan, to be paid in one lump sum; (4) The aforementioned 30 sets of films are rotated in six groups and shown in each institution or school. The order of precedence is determined by the Nanjing General Association of the Chinese Educational Film Association; (5) The round-trip postage for the films shall be borne by the institution or school renting the films. If two or more institutions or schools in the same place rent the aforementioned films at the same time, the postage shall be borne jointly by the two or more institutions or schools in the place; (6) The institution or school renting the films shall take care to protect the films. If there is any damage, compensation shall be paid according to the price.

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to Allocate Huge Funds to Expand Local Education in Jiangxi Province

(Nanchang Correspondence) The Jiangxi Provincial Government stipulates that all counties with education funding of more than 16,000 yuan shall establish an education bureau to handle the educational administration affairs of the county. Those that do not meet the stipulated standards shall abolish the bureau and merge it into a section, and establish a county school inspectorate under the county government to handle educational administration. In the bandit suppression area, due to the tightening of financial resources, there are also those who are abolished. In total, there are twenty-seven counties in the province that have established education bureaus, and thirty-five counties that have established county school inspectorates without education bureaus. In addition, most of the counties have been reduced to bandit areas, and education has come to a standstill. Now, in accordance with the special education implementation plan in the bandit suppression area, we are assisting various bandit suppression troops in carrying out the plan in earnest. According to the statistics of the 20th year, the total county education funding in the province is only 740,000 yuan. According to the statistics of the 21st year, the total local education funding for primary schools in the provincial capital and various counties and towns in the province is only 1,688,270 yuan and 3 dimes. The most is for elementary education in the provincial capital, 318,044 yuan and 8 jiao. The least is for Le'an County, only 600 yuan. Therefore, the local education funding in Jiangxi Province is extremely depleted. It is heard that Chairman Chiang Kai-shek will allocate huge funds to expand local education in Jiangxi Province.
