Women's National Goods Year Committee Sends Letter to Female Students in Various Schools Soliciting Essays

Deadline is the 15th of this Month

Cash Prizes and Gifts Will Be Awarded

Since its establishment, the Women's National Goods Movement Committee has actively promoted national goods, sparing no effort. The association has also launched an essay competition, with a deadline of the 15th of this month. On the 15th, it will also inspect various national goods manufacturers, and at the same time actively hold the Shanghai East District National Goods Exhibition, which is scheduled to open on the 18th. The details are recorded below:

Letter to Various Schools: The association sent a letter to major middle schools and universities, saying, "Respectfully, our association, in order to guide women to use domestic goods, practice what we preach, and prevent leakage and reverse the downward trend, is holding an essay competition from March 1st, soliciting excellent works from students in universities and middle schools. Various factories will prepare bonuses and prizes and invite celebrities to evaluate the quality of the essays, and those who rank high will be awarded cash or gifts to encourage them. We have long admired your school for its abundant talent and enthusiasm for protecting domestic goods. Therefore, we are sending a special letter to solicit contributions, and we have attached five copies each of the essay guidelines and essay topics. We hope you will check and inform the students to actively contribute, and please select good papers and send them to the association on time for evaluation and publication. This is what we earnestly pray for."

Essay Guidelines: The essay guidelines say, "(1) This essay is limited to female students in middle schools and universities. The principal of each school should first select good works and send them to the association with a letter. Each school is limited to a maximum of five papers; (2) This essay should be based on the student's own position, and the contribution of practical and feasible methods is qualified. Please do not send long-winded empty theories that are not helpful in practice; (3) This essay must be written in regular script, whether classical Chinese or vernacular Chinese, but it must be punctuated with new-style punctuation and must be written on domestic goods paper; (4) This essay must include the name, origin, age, school grade, and detailed mailing address; (5) This essay will be accepted from March 1st to March 15th. Late submissions will not be accepted; (6) After the association's essay deadline, we will invite seven gentlemen, Pan Gongzhan, Huang Renzhi, Wang Yunwu, Yan Esheng, Chen Diexian, Nie Tai, and Cai Jie Min's wife, to evaluate the quality of the essays and publish them in various newspapers on April 1st; (7) The selected essays will be awarded cash and products by various factories, and the association will award prizes according to the order of ranking; (8) Please send your contributions to the Essay Department of the China National Goods Production and Sales Cooperation Association, Yuanyuan Road (be sure to indicate the word "Essay" on the envelope)". Essay topics: "(1) How to fulfill the mission of the Women's National Goods Year; (2) What I should do for the Women's National Goods Year (choose one topic to complete the paper)".

The Bureau of Public Works Considers Increasing Tuition Fees for Various Schools

The Chief of the Finance Department of the Bureau of Public Works recently submitted a memorandum to the Education Committee, stating that the expenses of the Bureau of Public Works schools have always been borne separately by the parents of the students and the taxpayers. As for the proportion of their respective responsibilities, a principle was established several years ago that the tuition fees collected should account for one-third. To this day, the bureau's middle schools generally maintain this proportion, but if one were to investigate, it can be seen that this method actually makes the benefits received by the general parents far exceed the amount they bear. For example, suppose there is a foreigner A, who has two children in school, and pays a total of about 312 yuan in tuition fees per year. At the same time, the education fee borne by the donation tax on his behalf is 624 yuan. Suppose this person's monthly rent is 140 yuan, and the total donation paid per year is only 235 yuan and 2 jiao. Suppose there is a Chinese B, who has two children in the bureau's middle school, and pays about 153 yuan and 6 jiao in tuition fees per year, then the education fee paid by the donation tax on his behalf is about 307 yuan and 2 jiao. If this person's monthly rent is 80 yuan, then the total donation paid per year is only 134 yuan. From this point of view, the parents of the upper class not only have to have their education expenses supplemented by donation taxes, but also do not actually bear any of the other municipal expenses.

In other countries, the cost of education is borne by the public, but the situation in the Bureau of Public Works is different. The Bureau of Public Works does not have the right to compulsory education, and the children attending the bureau's schools are only a very small part of the school-age children in the boundary. In this way, a small number of citizens are obviously enjoying special preferential benefits that are borne by others, and most of the poor Chinese citizens are difficult to enjoy the convenience of this education.

The tuition fees of the bureau's schools are also related to non-bureau schools. The Bureau of Public Works encourages residents of various countries to run schools on their own, but the bureau's school fees are too low, which has an impact on competition with other schools. In view of the above reasons, the Chief of the Finance Department advocated that this issue should be considered immediately, so that the bureau's schools can uniformly increase tuition fees. After discussion by the Education Committee, it was considered extremely important and the memorandum has been copied and presented to the directors for review and published for public consideration.

Art Specialty Exhibition Closes Yesterday

Ye Gongchuo, Chen Lifu, and Others Visited

Mayor Wu Highly Praised All Exhibits

The fourth exhibition held by the National Hangzhou Art College at No. 11 Huanlong Road concluded as scheduled yesterday (the 9th) at 5 p.m. A total of over 560 pieces were exhibited this time. By the end of the exhibition, numerous verbal and written requests for extending the exhibition period were still being received. However, due to funding and time constraints, the association was unable to extend the exhibition any further and had already packed the exhibits separately in preparation for returning to Hangzhou.

Essays

Various Ways of "Setting Up"

— Shen Shouruo

The word "set up," when carefully examined, distinctly reveals the opposition between the two major classes of "laborers" and "aristocrats." It also allows one to appreciate that while there are differences in hardship, toil, and ease within the same act of setting up, the inherent risks do not vary accordingly.

In order to sustain a miserable life and prolong existence in harsh environments, one has no choice but to set up a stall to earn meager profits, barely enough to feed oneself or one's entire family. However, one often faces unexpected and severe interference, preventing the stable operation of the stall that sustains one's livelihood. With no other option, one must endure the pain and adopt a mobile approach, setting up here and there like engaging in clandestine activities. The heart sways restlessly like a pendulum.

Risking one's life in the dangerous swaying ferry across the Huangpu River is nothing more than an attempt to earn a few coins to buy food and nourish the five viscera. But how terrifying it is! The river surface is teeming with large ships like whales opening their giant mouths. A moment of carelessness could result in the small sampan being swallowed up at any time. Moreover, there might be unforeseen disasters; a sudden gust of wind could arise in the center of the river, and then the fate of the ferryman would be uncertain.

Setting up an official, grandiose, and seemingly inviolable facade forces those who worship such facades to bow deeply. At that moment, one not only feels both triumphant and carefree, but even those benevolent individuals who despise posturing, while cursing you, actually contribute to your aristocratic grandeur by stimulating the nerves of the blindly obedient. However, one must be careful not to overdo the facade, lest the structure collapse under its own weight.

The more items displayed on the table, the more extravagant the scene appears. However, I believe that those who are truly wealthy should feel free to display lavishly and extravagantly. Even if it leads to financial ruin, it could be seen as a form of social relief (because directly begging for help from those who cannot even afford the basic necessities of life is, of course, rarely granted). Conversely, those who lack the means but wish to create an illusion of grandeur may receive temporary praise as "young masters," but they must be cautious; hoodlums and thugs are often the veterans of such "young master" lifestyles.

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast Army

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Five: Tears Stream Down as a Woman Bids Farewell to Her Family to Serve in the Distant Borderlands; Throughout the Night, They March Out to Garrison a Lonely City

"Before, they said we only consumed grain without contributing to the nation. This time, we are finally serving the Republic of China, but we are still eating cornbread and drinking ice water." Ziqiang smiled and said, "We officers are considered fortunate; we even have an earthen platform to sleep on." Just as he was speaking, there was a rustling sound from the room next door. It turned out that it was a larger room, covered with straw on the ground, where the soldiers were all sleeping. Their movements caused the straw to rustle. Ziqiang said, "More than ten days ago, the battalion commander said we could receive wartime supplies. Why haven't they arrived yet after all this time?" Guan Yaowu said, "Who knows? Now, the whole country is saying that we are a non-resistance army, perhaps because of that. I curse the people who say we are not resisting! Why don't they come to the northeast and resist? If they only came here and tasted this hardship!" As he spoke, he stomped his foot forcefully on the ground. Ziqiang laughed and said, "Old Guan, why are you complaining?" Before he could reply, there was a loud crash, and dust from the roof of the room rained down like chaff. Guan Yaowu, being an experienced veteran, had already jumped out of the room. Ziqiang, fearing something unexpected had happened, immediately drew his pistol from its holster and followed him outside. Then they heard someone shouting, "The wind has blown down the house!" Zhao Ziqiang calmed himself down, recalling that the sound did indeed seem like a house collapsing. He immediately stood outside the door of the soldiers' quarters, suppressing any commotion. After a short while, there was another loud crash, and several more houses collapsed. Listening to the wind in the sky, sometimes roaring for a long time, sometimes howling, it continued to intensify. During a march, especially when encountering unexpected weather, it is crucial to maintain vigilance to prevent accidents. The battalion commander had already issued orders to increase precautions. Wang Shili walked up to Ziqiang and said in a low voice, "Company commander, the house you are staying in is also creaking and groaning. I'm afraid it will collapse. We must be extra careful tonight." (332)

Nanjing Road Thirty Years Ago

— Qing Qu

Nanjing Road, which is now the first major road in the British Concession, is known to anyone who has visited Shanghai for its prosperity and liveliness. The towering buildings on both sides are like distant jade palaces and lofty green cities, while the vehicles moving east and west in the middle are like shuttles weaving back and forth day and night. Shanghai is hardly a major city in the world, but in China, it is like Venice or Florence in medieval Italy! It began as a mere commercial gathering, but gradually developed countless related historical events.

Thirty years ago, the most famous section of Nanjing Road extended from the Bund Park in the east to the Bowling Green in the west. Beyond that, weeds grew wild, white poplars rustled in the wind, few people traveled there, and distinguished guests rarely visited. The "Rainbow Temple" was just a dilapidated building, and aside from the old women who burned incense and candles, there were few young women dressed in finery, accompanied by teenage girls, kneeling at the feet of the Buddhas. The "British Municipal Council" was located in Pintang Lane, but its authority was not as extensive or strict as it is today. It is said that when "Zuo Zongtang" was transferring troops to Zhejiang, he led several thousand soldiers through Shanghai, still armed with rifles, marching directly along Nanjing Road. The foreigners not only dared not interfere but also had to salute them!

The most famous and earliest-established theater in Shanghai was "Sanya Garden," located near today's Wing On Department Store. One day, the strongman "Ma Yongzhen" performed there, and the ticket price, which was originally only ten cents, was increased to forty cents, which was considered unprecedented. Later, Ma was killed by a horse dealer at "Yidongtian," located in Daxin Street, to the left of Wankang Sauce Garden before the revolution. A corner of the small building still remained, with the inscription "Yidongtian." North of Nicheng Bridge was the "Foreign Affairs Bureau." Whenever the Shanghai Daotai went out of the city to attend to matters at the bureau, he would pass through Nanjing Road, riding in a carriage, preceded by a mounted military officer, flanked by guards, and followed by two attendants on horseback, making a grand procession through the city. The scenic spot "Yangliu Loutai" was founded by the first person to create the "Youxi Bao" newspaper, named "Xiangfu," a grandson of Yuan Zicai, who used the pseudonym "Yangliu Loutai Master." Now, I fear no one remembers him. In the racecourse, there was also a "stone archway," a relic that a certain family had not sold to foreigners. In the past, descendants would come to sweep the tombs during Qingming, but now, I fear they are scattered and lost. Who knows if the spirits of their ancestors are still watching over them! "North of the Racecourse" and "East of Longfei Horse Stable" was a tall Western-style building with a teahouse called "Zhezhe Lou" on the upper floor. Its owner was a Cantonese named "Shi Dezhi." Few people could understand the meaning of the two words "Zhezhe," because they were inscribed by the famous "Wo Fo Shanren," and were therefore extraordinary. In fact, they meant "The benevolent see benevolence, the wise see wisdom." Once explained, everyone understood!

Just recalling Nanjing Road has made me feel as if I have experienced great changes, all like a dream. What more can I say? It shows that the singing stages and dance pavilions of today may become overgrown with weeds in the future, and the drunken revelry of tonight may end up in a three-inch coffin!

Handshake and Bow

— Li Taoan

There are many differences between Western and Chinese etiquette. For example, when people in Europe and America meet, they shake hands to show intimacy, but in our ancient country, it is somewhat different, with people cupping their hands and bowing deeply to each other. (Although some modern people have already changed this.)

In fact, this is just a superficial politeness, and there is nothing really important about it. However, a friend said that from this very small occasion, one can see the differences in the expressions of various national characteristics. Foreigners are more unified and communal, so everyone becomes one when they meet. Speaking of ourselves, we have always boasted of the old saying "Each sweeps the snow from his own doorstep, and cares not for the frost on others' roofs," so when we meet each other, we merely cup our hands and bow from a distance.

But I believe that this statement is just a humorous anecdote. If it were true, it would not only be insulting to our own people, but it would also be very unfair to them.

Shenbao Radio Weekly

The Most Economical Vacuum Tube Tester

— Guo Yongnian

A vacuum tube tester is an instrument for testing whether various vacuum tubes can work under normal conditions. Ready-made products may not be available domestically; even if they are, the price will certainly be exorbitantly high, beyond the reach of the average person. This article introduces a simple and economical version. Small-scale radio research groups or individual hobbyists should all make one to have a definite judgment on the quality of vacuum tubes when building or repairing radios. The components shown in the diagram are explained below:

Filament Transformer: Used with 110V AC power. The core is made of one-inch wide silicon steel sheets stacked to a thickness of one inch in a "mountain" shape. The primary winding uses No. 28 enameled wire wound 660 turns. The secondary winding uses No. 16 enameled wire wound a total of 45 turns, with taps at the 9th, 15th, 18th, 30th, and 45th turns, providing five different filament voltages: 1.5V, 2.5V, 3V, 5V, and 7.5V. The lead wires are connected to terminal posts. Adjacent terminal posts must be far apart, or an un wired terminal post should be installed between two wired ones to prevent the switch from simultaneously contacting two terminal posts when changing the voltage. Otherwise, the secondary winding may easily burn out. Each terminal should be labeled with its respective voltage to prevent errors. A is a milliampere meter, with a range of 0-10 mA being sufficient.

Rl is a shunt resistor for A, and by closing SW·r, one can know that a current three times larger than the indication of A is passing through. The resistance value is 900 ohms.

R2 is a 50-ohm center-tapped resistor.

R3 is a 500-ohm resistor that generates a 1.5V C voltage.

R4 has 3500 ohms. Together with R3, it can generate a 4-volt C voltage. The remaining two are an X-type four-pin tube socket and a Y-type five-pin tube socket.

The first time it is used, various known vacuum tubes that can serve as standards should be plugged into this tester, the power turned on, and the filament voltage adjusted. First close SW2, then release it, and the maximum and minimum values can be read on the meter. After each type of vacuum tube has been tested in this way, a table can be created, and the numbers in this table can be used as a basis for judgment in the future.

Highest Reading 668810941058

Lowest Reading 2122221212

Vacuum Tube -10-27-26-71-12-45-99-80-24-22

The attached table is for several common vacuum tubes, which readers can use as a reference. For No. 71 and 80, SW·I must be closed to prevent excessive current from passing through A. The same applies to all vacuum tubes with high plate current. For tetrodes such as No. 24, an additional base must be added to make the connector shown in Figure 2. When in use, plug the lamp holder of the connector into the lamp holder of the tester, plug the vacuum tube into the lamp holder of the connector, and clamp the steel sheet onto the G pole on the top of the vacuum tube to test in the same way.

Talking About Batteries for Radios

— Ming Xiang

For DC radios, the power supply almost entirely relies on batteries. Batteries that cannot be restored after being used up are called primary cells. Those that can be charged with external power to restore their function are called secondary cells or storage cells. Primary cells include the commonly used dry batteries, as well as the newly introduced air cells. Storage cells also have lead-acid and Edison types. Here is a brief explanation of each:

Dry Batteries: Dry batteries are not really dry. Their construction is as follows: A carbon rod in the center serves as the positive electrode, and a cylindrical zinc can on the outside serves as the negative electrode. The two electrodes are separated by a mixture of manganese dioxide and other anti-depolarizing agents, as well as water-absorbing paper separators, all soaked in a solution of zinc chloride and ammonium chloride to initiate a chemical reaction. Each cell has a voltage of 1.5 volts. If they are used to supply the A voltage for lighting the filaments of radios, several can be connected in series, and a bleeder resistor can be used to adjust it to match the filament voltage of the vacuum tubes. However, their capacity is limited and they cannot be restored, so it is best to use the storage batteries mentioned below for radios with a total filament current of more than half an ampere, which is more economical. Many small dry batteries can also be combined to provide the B voltage for the plate power of vacuum tubes.

Air Cells: This type of battery is named because its anti-depolarizing agent directly obtains oxygen from the surrounding air. Each cell has a voltage of about 2.5 volts when first used and a very large capacity of 600 ampere-hours, making it most suitable for supplying the filaments of 2-volt vacuum tubes (such as 230, 232, 233, etc.). However, its discharge rate cannot exceed 0.75 amperes, and it is also more expensive, so it is not widely seen in the Chinese market.

Lead-Acid Storage Batteries: These batteries use lead electrodes immersed in a dilute sulfuric acid solution with a specific gravity of 1.280. An external DC current is then passed through, entering from the positive lead electrode and exiting from the negative electrode, causing the active material of the positive electrode (i.e., the material that initiates the chemical reaction) to become brown lead dioxide and the negative electrode to become bluish-gray spongy lead. A fully charged battery has a voltage of about 2.2 volts. Storage batteries for providing the A voltage to radios are connected in series with three cells to form a battery with a voltage of 6 volts and a capacity of about 60 ampere-hours to 200 ampere-hours. Connecting many lead-acid storage batteries with very small capacities in series to serve as the B voltage for radios is also very suitable, because they can be revived by external power after being used up, making them inexhaustible and particularly economical. However, managing and carrying them is more troublesome.

Edison Batteries: Invented by Thomas Edison, their construction is roughly similar to that of lead-acid batteries, but all containers, electrodes, etc., are made of cast steel. The active material of the positive electrode is nickel hydroxide, the negative electrode is iron oxide, and the electrolyte is a dilute solution of potassium hydroxide. When the battery is fully charged, each cell has a voltage of about 1.2 volts. Their special advantages are that they are sturdy and durable. Even if they are short-circuited, shelved, or shaken, their lifespan will not be reduced, and they are light in weight and have low maintenance costs, but because they are very expensive, they are not very popular.

A Powerful Single-Tube Radio Using a 33 Detector

— Wang Fumin

In ordinary radios, triodes or tetrodes are mostly used for detection, but now we can also use a low-frequency power pentode for detection. Do you find it amazing? Using it to make a one-tube radio can indeed surpass everything. Circuits of this kind have also been published in other radio publications. The circuit introduced here is similar to others, but an additional variable condenser and coil L3 are added next to L4, which can increase the selectivity of the radio. The required parts are listed below:

L1: Use a 30mm diameter bakelite tube and wind 50 turns of No. 26 double cotton-covered wire. It must be able to change its inductance.

L1L2L3L4: Use a 30mm diameter bakelite tube and wind No. 26 double cotton-covered wire. First wind 10 turns for L1, then 55 turns for L2, then 45 turns for L4. The three coils are separated by 8.2mm.

L3: Wind 50 turns of the same wire on the outside of L4. The two coils must be separated by insulation.

C3: 0.00045 mfd variable condenser

C: 0.00045 mfd variable condenser

Cl: 0.00025 mfd fixed condenser

R: 3 megolun fixed resistor

C2: 0.00035mfd mica or variable condenser

Use a storage battery for the A voltage, because the 33 filament consumes 0.26 amperes, which is very power-consuming. The B voltage can be gradually tested from 45 volts to 90 volts to see which voltage produces the loudest sound.

On Capacitors

— Meng Cheng

The capacitor is one of the most important components in electrical instruments, and an indispensable part of radio circuits. In radios, whether it is an amplifier, detector, rectifier, oscillator, or crystal radio circuit, capacitors must be connected in order to be effective.

Two conductors separated by an insulator and not connected form a capacitor, because if a voltage is applied between the two plates, a considerable amount of charge will be stored on the two plates after a very short time. Two wires separated by a few centimeters in the air also form a capacitor, because air is an insulator. When a voltage is applied, charge is stored on the wires, but the amount of charge stored at this time is very small and generally not noticed. The insulator between the conductors is specifically called the dielectric, and air, waxed paper, mica, and oils are all good and commonly used dielectrics.

The resistance of a capacitor to alternating current is inversely proportional to the frequency of the alternating current. Direct current can be said to be a special case of alternating current, with its frequency being zero, so the resistance of a capacitor to direct current is infinite. In other words, direct current cannot pass through a capacitor, and a capacitor can separate alternating current and direct current. Because the resistance is inversely proportional to the frequency, a capacitor can also separate high-frequency alternating current from low-frequency alternating current. The functions of bypass capacitors and filter capacitors are based on the above principles.

Capacitors are classified into two types according to their structure: fixed and variable. Fixed capacitors mostly use mica or oil paper as the dielectric, and variable capacitors mostly use air as the dielectric. According to their different functions in the radio, fixed capacitors are further divided into grid capacitors, bypass capacitors, and filter capacitors, etc. Grid capacitors are used for the temporary storage of electrons on the grid, and their capacitance is very small. Bypass capacitors are used to facilitate the flow of high-frequency currents, and their capacitance is relatively large, while filter capacitors are used to short-circuit low-frequency currents, and their capacitance is even larger. Variable capacitors are mostly used in tuning circuits, but some are also used to control oscillation. Their capacitance is always very small, about tens to hundreds of picofarads. There are also several identical variable capacitors combined on one axis for convenient tuning, called coaxial capacitors.

On Loudspeakers

— Zhu Ziyuan

A loudspeaker, commonly known as a horn or speaker, is a device that can emit sounds loud enough for many people to hear after receiving an audio current. They vary in type and construction. Here, let's briefly talk about a few common types.

The first type is the steel diaphragm loudspeaker. Its principle and construction are completely similar to those of a receiver, but all materials are enlarged to strengthen the electromagnetic force, causing the diaphragm to vibrate more violently, resulting in a louder sound. Adding a horn on top completes the assembly, as shown in Figure 1. M is a horseshoe-shaped permanent magnet. Coils Cr and C2 are wound with fine copper wire on the two magnetic poles S and N in series. The diaphragm is placed above the magnetic poles, with a very small gap in between. When a low-frequency current passes through these two coils, it generates a magnetic force of varying intensity depending on the strength of the current, which in turn affects the change in the magnetic force of the permanent magnet, causing the diaphragm above the magnet to vibrate up and down. The amplitude and speed of the vibration vary according to the strength of the magnetic force, and the surrounding air is agitated to produce sound.

In this type of loudspeaker, the distance between the diaphragm and the magnetic poles is extremely difficult to adjust properly. If it is too close, the diaphragm will easily come into contact with the magnetic poles and produce noise when the sound is loud. If it is too far, faint sounds cannot be heard. Moreover, its effectiveness varies for different frequencies, and there is often the disadvantage of having a resonant frequency, resulting in an excessively high sound at a certain frequency. Therefore, there are now very few users of this type.

When using this type of loudspeaker, pay attention to the following points:

(1) Do not use strong shocks.

(2) The positive and negative terminals should not be connected in reverse (connect the colored wire to B+).

(3) Do not allow dust to enter the speaker.

(4) Prevent moisture.

(5) The distance between the magnetic poles and the diaphragm must be adjusted.

The second type is the so-called balanced-armature loudspeaker, which is an evolution of the steel-diaphragm loudspeaker. Its sensitivity is limited to high frequencies, and it avoids contact with the magnetic poles when the sound is loud. Its construction is roughly as follows:

A is a tongue made of soft iron, on the outside of which thousands of turns of fine copper wire are wound. It is then placed between the iron pieces in magnet D. When a low-frequency current passes through the coil, the tongue becomes magnetic. Due to the principles of like poles repelling and opposite poles attracting, the magnetic force of the permanent magnet alternately attracts and repels the tongue. The tongue vibrates left and right with M as the center (Figure 2). The rod B transmits this vibration to the diaphragm C, agitating the air to produce sound.

When using this type of loudspeaker, the position of the tongue must be in the center of the two poles to allow it to vibrate freely. The rest is the same as above.

The above two types are both electromagnetic loudspeakers. There is also a type called a dynamic loudspeaker, which is very popular on AC radios now. Its general construction is as follows:

Direct Current Excitation - Output Transformer Connection

A is wrought iron, B is the moving magnetic coil, D is the voice coil (also called the moving coil) connected to the diaphragm. The excitation coil is supplied with direct current (in AC radios, it is often used as a filtering choke coil). The voice coil is connected to the output transformer. When direct current flows through the excitation coil, the wrought iron becomes an electromagnet. At the same time, when a low-frequency current passes through the voice coil, it also becomes a magnetic field. Due to the interaction of the two magnetic fields, the voice coil vibrates. The strength of the vibration varies depending on the sound current and the excitation current. The excitation current is usually from tens of milliamperes to several amperes. Of course, if the excitation current is larger, better results can be obtained, but it is also necessary to estimate whether the excitation coil can withstand a larger current, otherwise it will heat up and burn out. After the voice coil is vibrated, because it is connected to the diaphragm C, the diaphragm is also vibrated, thus agitating the air to create sound.

When using this type of loudspeaker, if the DC voltage of the excitation coil is insufficient, the sound will be weak. If there is no sound, in addition to a break in the speaker wire or loose connections, a broken wire in the excitation coil should also be noted.

A Collection of News

Successful Ultra-Shortwave Communication Across the Strait: The British Lympne radio station and the French Saint Inglevert airfield radio station have begun formal communication using 17 and 19-meter ultra-short waves. The antenna used is directional, with a power of 500 watts. Both stations use teleprinters for automatic transmission and reception. It is said that there is absolutely no static interference with this wavelength. (One Knowledge)

World's First Successful Ultra-Shortwave Telephone: Ultra-shortwave telephone communication has been used between the Hawaiian Islands in the United States. This wave has been used by experimenters in various countries and has a length of about several meters, but it is not the microwave of 50 centimeters used by Marconi.

The Hawaiian Islands are located in a sea area with rapid currents, so in 1912, the Honolulu Telephone Bureau planned to use submarine cables to connect to the island, but failed due to the difficulty of the work. Afterwards, it used medium-length waves to communicate with the island, but due to the surrounding hot air and severe static interference, it was difficult to talk.

Since 1928, experimenters have used ultra-shortwave telephone communication. Last year, the telephone bureau had equipped transmitters and receivers to communicate with various islands. Users are connected from telephone lines to a switching exchange, and then transmitted by ultra-shortwave transmitters. This ultra-shortwave wireless telephone is very secret because the radio waves travel in a straight line, so the transmitter and receiver must use antennas in the same direction to receive it. (One Knowledge)

Free Talk

On the Detestable Nature of Laughter

— Lin Yutang

This happened one night in a café. The reason was that Ya Xi had just returned from France. That evening, he heard his uncle, Xiangfu, praise the elegance and interest of the cafés on Avenue Joffre, speaking highly of them. To Ya Xi, it seemed that he was saying that the cafés in Paris were not good, which he resented. He defiantly invited his old classmate, Yu Jun, and his uncle to come with him. In Xiangfu's pronunciation, Ya Xi was pronounced somewhat peculiarly. To Lao Yu, it sounded like Ya Sai, and the word "Sai" seemed to be read in the first tone. When he was studying in France, he had spelled his name in four ways: Asen, Asay, Asailles, and Asaient, especially the last two, which he was most proud of. However, since a French girl called him Assez, his classmates also called him Ssez, and some translated it into Chinese, calling him "Enough." Still others translated it into classical Chinese, calling him "Alas." There were also students who had studied in England who came to visit Paris and called him Isay. However, Xiangfu, because he had been used to calling him A Sai since he was a child, still called him A Sai, and the word "Sai" was read in the first tone. Ya Xi had no choice but to say that he had recently returned to China and that his nickname was really not very pleasant. Ya Xi was his style name, but his uncle still did not think it was necessary to call his nephew by his style name.

The three of them were sitting at a table near mine. Ya Xi saw that there was a glass surface on the table and thought that Shanghai had indeed progressed in the few years he had been abroad, but he was not willing to praise domestic products easily.

"Look at that woman's permed hair, trying to imitate Paris, neither East nor West, it's really too humorous."

"Do you even understand this new term, 'humor'?" Lao Yu said.

"How could I not understand! I've read a few 'Analects' in Paris... What a joke! Chinese people don't understand humor at all!"

Xiangfu was originally also a moralist. He had always been against humor. But what he opposed was not buffoonery, but the Western term "humor," especially the use of the two words "Analects" as the name of a publication by modern people. He said that buffoonery and absurdity were harmless, and that it was harmless for literati to occasionally write some playful words as a pastime. He was against buffoonery that also spoke serious words, both solemn and humorous. He said that, for example, if a man wanted to visit a prostitute, he should go outside to do so. Is it appropriate to kiss and behave indecently with his own wife? Imagine if the wife at home also played the huqin, sang Peking opera, permed her hair, and dressed up flamboyantly, what a scandal it would be. He was very serious and upright at home, and the children at home could not see his romantic side. Therefore, he always looked at the "Analects" with a stern face, getting angrier the more he read, although he read it more and more angrily. The "Analects" has always been bought up by this group of people who are filled with righteous indignation and "look at it angrily"; Lao Yu's generation often cannot buy it, or if they do, it is confiscated by the old man at home. But at this moment, because Ya Xi was against it, he wanted to say a few good words for domestic products, because although Ya Xi had studied abroad, in his eyes, he was still A Sai, and the word "Sai" was read in the first tone.

"What's wrong with the 'Analects'?" Xiangfu said.

At this time, Uncle Xiangfu was in favor of humor, while Ya Xi had become a moralist; this alignment was a bit peculiar.

"Something like La Vie Parisienne is humorous, makes you laugh uncontrollably," I was looking at a picture in La Vie Parisienne at the time, a pair of women's legs placed on the bulging belly of a doughy rich man 丨丨 "That's that subtle, relaxed laughter of the Latin people. Just like this café, it makes you uncomfortable sitting here. When I was in Paris, I could sit in a café for half a day. I don't know why, it makes you feel that a toothy smile under a Latin mustache is appropriate. We Chinese people don't grow our mustaches well. Chinese laughter is also detestable."

Xiangfu had a mustache. Hearing these words, he glared at him sharply. Lao Yu saw that the situation was not good and quickly changed the subject.

"Ya Xi, I haven't been to Paris, but I've seen a lot of French mustaches on Avenue Joffre. I don't think it's that big a deal. I don't think that Westerners are necessarily so superior when they laugh, and Chinese people are necessarily so detestable. The 'Analects' also translated a piece of French humor called 'The Scholar and the Thief' in issue 28, which looks no different from the 'Collection of Jokes.' You're all just a bunch of dogmatic moralists."

"You're mistaken. It was published in issue 30 of the 'Analects,' not issue 28," said Ya Xi, who had just returned from studying in France. "I read it on the French mail ship Bordes on my way back from Europe."

"You're both wrong. 'The Scholar and the Thief' was in issue 26, published on October 1st. I happened to be going to Wuxi that day and bought it on the train. It was clearly October 1st, how could I be mistaken?"

I drank a large cup of coffee and left. In my heart, I was thinking: 28? 26? 30? I really couldn't remember clearly, and I wasn't even sure if issue 26 was published on October 1st. When I got home, I looked for my collection of books, but couldn't find it anywhere. I had issues 27 to 30, but none of them had that article "The Scholar and the Thief." Unfortunately, issue 26 was missing. I called the Times Company and asked them to send someone to deliver issue 26 immediately. The people at the Times were panicked, thinking that something had gone wrong with issue 26. I said, "Nothing, I'm just having a nervous breakdown. The people who are against it have remembered the issue numbers clearly, but I can't remember them. I wish everyone in the world was against humor."

"What!?" came a startled voice on the phone.

"Send someone to deliver issue 26 immediately," I abruptly hung up the phone.

A Request for an Explanation of the Xu He Creation Issue

— Liang Xin

There are always new things happening in the current "literary world," but most of them are not good things. The "plagiarism" and "cutting and pasting" cases are long gone, but the new year has brought the creative issue of Mr. He Jiahai. This issue seems to have been going on for quite a long time in other newspapers, but there have only been two mentions of it in this publication. But after reading Mr. Shi Heng's article, it is clear that this issue is not as simple as "cutting and pasting."

The scope of this issue is relatively large. The locations are Nanjing Houhu, Shanghai, and the hometown of Mr. Xu Zhuanpeng (I don't know where it is); the people involved are two protagonists, Shi Heng, "Cleaner," Chu Anping, Gao Zhi, Shen Congwen, Shi Zhicun, Shao Xunmei, Du Heng, and Mr. Cunren, making it a lively affair unprecedented in all previous cases. The evidence includes the owner's conversations, letters, the difference in writing style between He and Xu, and the original manuscripts that can be printed in the future, which is enough to go to the extreme.

Readers could have already made a conclusion. "Legal issues" will not succeed. Publishing it in the newspaper is just to tell the readers. However, Mr. Shi Heng's article, in addition to revealing the truth, also planted a doubt. He said: "However, Zhuanpeng has a different explanation, narrating the ins and outs, but without Zhuanpeng's permission, it is not convenient to disclose it now."

We know of two ways that people take other people's articles and claim them as their own. One is to copy other people's works and submit them to newspapers. We often see authors or readers subsequently exposing them. The other is to buy other people's translations cheaply, change the names to their own, and sell them at a higher price. We also often hear rumors about this. But this time, the author's article was stolen, and there is also an explanation. Mr. Shi Heng stood up for responsibility, but it is "not convenient to disclose" the explanation, so we only know part of the "scandal." What is the reason for this?

To expose a scandal, it must be exposed to the end. I long to know that explanation, but of course, it is only entirely out of curiosity, and also to add some knowledge to the literary world.

At Mount Madeta

— Hei Ying

Climbing along the rugged, winding mountain road, the car roared as if it was tired. The day was bright and clear, and when we arrived, we all felt hot, but when we stopped by the spring halfway up the mountain and jumped out of the car, the wind was much cooler.

(What a miracle! On the island of Sumatra on the equator, there is such a cool Mount Madeta. It is autumn all year round; I have been there twice, and I know that I should put on a light wool sweater now.)

Standing on the hillside, looking out over the distant ground, the houses and coconut groves make up a landscape oil painting. Looking further, the blue sea connects with the sky. I breathed a sigh of relief and quietly praised in my heart:

丨Beautiful southern island!

X　X　X　X

Taking Ya Zhen, I walked briskly on the smooth road; this little girl looked at the Madeta people with curious eyes, looking at the houses where the Madeta people lived. Passing a small stream, many children were swimming naked; the weather here is autumn, but they can still jump into the stream!

The scenery is almost the same as elsewhere, with coconut trees everywhere. However, there are deep green wildernesses and sulfur mountains that are constantly spewing gas. This is the old home of the Madeta people, and their style is different from that of the Malays.

On this day, not far from where we lived, the Madeta people's opera was being performed. Ya Zhen was clamoring to see it, but I hated those things. Now we walked to the outskirts, and a gust of wind carrying the melancholy smell of wildflowers blew on my face, and I leaned closely against her on the grass all afternoon as if I was drunk.

X　X　X　X

In the evening, Mount Madeta was silent.

I felt lonely. Ya Zhen was taken to the house by her mother to sleep, leaving me alone, sitting, sitting, the night was quiet.

X　X　X　X

Early in the morning, before the sunlight shone down, I got out of bed. Without washing my face, I stood in front of the window and looked out at a layer of hazy morning mist. The sulfur mountain was completely covered by fog, and in front of me was a gray haze...

The sunlight shone through the gray mist onto the bed, and I straightened my tie.

丨GoodMarning

Like a little bird, she jumped to the clothes rack, brought me a coat, and walked closer to me. I liked Ya Zhen's innocent smiling face.

(Should I give her a kiss? What a lovely girl!)

But I didn't stretch my mouth over; I went downstairs with her to eat breakfast.

Back home, I kept thinking about Mount Madeta; now I can't forget Mount Madeta. It is truly a miracle that on the island of Sumatra on the equator, there is such a cool Mount Madeta...

Random Notes on Returning South (Continued)

— Tang Tao

(2) Lamenting the Past

When I got home, I had some refreshments. My mother was the first to tell me some trivial family matters. Nothing has been right in the past few years. We lose hundreds of dollars every year on the fields. The wages of the helpers are equal to the wages of a clerk in a small shop, but they are still lazy and gluttonous, gambling until three in the morning, and then lying in bed during the day pretending to have a stomachache.

Since my father died, everyone in the village has become indifferent. Friends, of course, are out of the question, and even relatives have slipped away one by one. When a woman manages the household, she is bullied everywhere. Who is willing to say a fair word?

All of these things have added deep wrinkles to my mother's face, giving her a heavy cough in the morning and causing her to dream about prosperity, decline, and human warmth and coldness at night.

My mother asked me about my journey. My nephews and nieces surrounded me, asking for comic books. I just thought silently, thinking that this family had a musty smell of decay, the courtyard was so deserted, I could almost find the footprints of weasels in every corner; there was an empty swallow's nest hanging on the beam; sparrows were nesting in the seams of the tiles; and gray-white lime and eroded wood chips often fell from the ceiling and pillars. Home, this is nothing like our home of a few years ago.

A few years ago, our house was always full of people. Although we were always poor at heart, we children were happy enough, jumping, laughing, fighting, and only adults hated us for being too noisy and unruly. Heaven knows, now it has become like this!

I ran upstairs, and loneliness followed me upstairs. Opening my suitcase, I wanted to find my childhood, my unruly jumping, laughing, and fighting. Here, there were piles and piles of my elementary school copybooks, dictation books, and composition books, white paper, black characters, worm-like strokes; I saw the Roman letters written in red ink after each article, one hundred points, ninety points; I remembered the joy of receiving the booklets from the teacher's hand. I remembered the lotus root fields planted along the river, and my two sisters and I carrying our schoolbags to school there every day. I remembered the image of Guan Gong, enlarged and painted from a illustrated novel and pasted on the gate. I remember everything, but nothing allows me to recall it again. The tree trunk on my eldest sister's grave has grown taller than a person, and my second sister's children can also read comic books and draw Guan Gong to paste on the gate.

I, myself, have become the supporter of this deserted courtyard.

My mother said that I was tired from the journey and advised me to sleep for a while. Lying on the bed in my old home, I dreamed of the prosperity of the past.

Dusk

— Jin Yi

Measuring the endless, quiet, and long days, Qingzhi and Qingsong's ages were both over thirty.

Although this does not count as reaching an age that only makes people sigh; but their hearts, year after year, are sinking into a state of aging. Coupled with a dim, unadorned, yellow face: on which are dry lips, and lifeless eyes surrounded by dark circles; they have also not worn bright clothes for a long time, and have slender bodies, walking with slow steps... Like these, can make people know, after seeing them for the first time, that they are only thirty-one years old, and let out a slight sigh: "Ah, they are only thirty-one years old!"

They are also silent, even when there are only two of them, they don't talk much; in front of people, they are almost like reclusive monks. When they really want to say something, they just let their lips move slightly. They engrave all events in their hearts.

Called sisters, they are twin sisters. The older sister, Qingzhi, came into this world half a day earlier than her younger sister, Qingsong. In appearance, behavior, and personality: they have great similarities. But in terms of encounters, Qingsong became a widow just three months after getting married; while Qingzhi is still an old maid who has not married.

Qingsong's marriage was in the year she was nineteen: the husband was a third-stage tuberculosis patient. Originally, she would not have married so early, because of a bit of truth in the legends of this ancient nation, saying that it could be useful, she turned Qingsong from a girl into a woman, and this period was only a short three months, and she became a widow without a husband again.

In her husband's house, in her own house: a widow must somehow spend her long years of widowhood alone. So, after guarding her mourning for a year in her husband's house, she was picked up by her wealthy father and returned to her mother's house.

Ah, this year, the only things that accompanied her day and night were tears and shadows, not because she was mourning the dead, but because she thought that even a young girl could only live a lonely life until the day she died, so beautiful things were just empty, and things that could arouse the interest of young people only made her frown even tighter. Her mother and sister often came to see her, and Qingbai, who was still studying, also came to accompany her on holidays, but this caused her greater sadness, that is, without overly sentimental leaning on her mother's shoulder or hugging her sister and crying bitterly, she would shed more tears. People with bone-deep affection, it is more difficult to endure the bitterness in their hearts.

Fluctuations within a Dollar or so

Increased New Buys on New York Stock Market

New Feng Foreign Firm reports: On the 8th, the New York stock market was still mixed and slightly lower. However, due to Roosevelt's new attitude towards airmail and good earnings reports from various companies, morale has shown a turning point. Later, the drafter of the Frazier-Lemke Farm Bankruptcy Act declared that the bill would be amended, including the relaxation of margin requirements. Transactions suddenly became active, shorts covered, and new buyers surged in, fearing being left behind. The current prices are indeed very cheap. The U.S. Treasury Department issued only 460 million dollars in treasury bonds this time, so U.S. government bonds were unusually strong, creating a new high price for the year. The small exchange market also rose, with a total of 1.7 million shares traded for the day. Wheat longs continued to sell off, brokers absorbed, benefiting the longs. Cotton had little fluctuation in the morning, but rose with the stock market in the afternoon due to the impending lenient amendment of the bill restricting speculation on the securities exchange. According to reports, the Soviet Union will purchase 500,000 bales of American cotton, and the financial community is willing to provide assistance, so it is indeed possible to realize. Opinions on the proposal to increase New York warehouse fees are becoming increasingly inconsistent. The May period has settled. The Dow Jones indices are listed below:

Yarn Retail Investors Inclined to Dump

The yarn market is weakening, and the situation is softening again. Because there is still no hope for a large-scale improvement in actual demand, and various businesses remain depressed, general retail investors are inclined to dump. However, foreign cotton is strong and rising. The amount absorbed by a certain manufacturer is not released. In short, the environment is bad. Although the base is depleted, it is still difficult to arouse buying interest.

In the pre-market opening for marked yarn, the market situation was still good because American cotton rose and the selling sentiment in the market was not strong. By the second and third bidding rounds, market prices tended to fall. As a result, the spot month rose by 30 cents, and the far month fell by 3, 4, and 60 cents. In the afternoon, because cotton was flat and tired, the yarn market fell again, with each month falling by 2, 5, 7, and 80 cents. The total number of transactions for the day was 13,800 bales. Tianjin Xihua Cotton Slightly Shows Signs of Life

Tianjin News: After a long period of stagnation, the Xihua cotton market is now beginning to show signs of life. Although there were contacts in the morning, they did not come to fruition. In the afternoon, a foreign merchant bought 269 bales, opening at 41.3 dollars. There were no other transactions. Grains Flour Prices Rebound Firmly in Afternoon Trading to Cover Short Positions

Yesterday in the flour market, after trading opened in the morning, prices for all months generally displayed a flat and weak trend. Due to the quotation for foreign wheat being better by about one jiao in Chicago, and better by varying amounts up to four fen in Canada, market sentiment was generally weak after the opening prices. It was confirmed by both government and private sources that the government wheat was being sold in large quantities. It is rumored that Fook and Foo corporations together have a total of seventeen ships, with seven ships remaining, which were purchased separately by small local factories and factories along the Yangtze River. The price was as low as $3.80. It is said that this special accommodation was made to compensate for losses due to the previously levied wheat tax. However, the market is currently sluggish, and factories are temporarily adopting a cautious approach. Therefore, although sentiment is weak, the declines have not been very large. The July contract only reached 2.025 yuan, close to the 2 yuan mark, while the other months mainly saw declines of just a few fen. When trading opened at noon, due to the market being short, there was eager covering of positions. Large factories were uniformly firm, with only small factories selling slightly, so prices rebounded. According to the current situation, prices may temporarily stabilize, but considering the decline in various commodity prices, there is little hope for a bright future. As a result, the current month was better by 2.5 li than the previous day, April was better by 5 li, May was better by 1 fen, June was better by 2.5 li, July was unchanged, and August was better by 5 li.

期麥清淡現麥步俏

Quiet Trading in Wheat Futures, Spot Wheat Gradually Gains Favor

Yesterday in the wheat futures market, after trading opened in both the morning and afternoon, prices for all months generally showed a stable trend. The quotation for foreign wheat was better by one jiao in Chicago, and better by four fen in Canada. After the opening prices, market sentiment remained stable. Although a large batch of government wheat has been traded, it is said that the exchange market had prior negotiations and agreed not to sell, so although the trend is not very good, there are also few sellers. Trading in each contract was as quiet as before, and this is the reason. The closing result was that only July was down by one fen, with no changes in the other months. In the spot wheat market, because arrivals and inventories are not abundant, and because factories mostly use foreign wheat, domestic wheat must be blended, so prices are gradually gaining favor. Kainan Suchow wheat was at 3.53 yuan, Shandong wheat at 2.51 yuan, and Bengbu wheat at 3.44 yuan, totaling 2,500 bags, which were handled by Fooshin Huafong Company.

蘇常白粳回好五分

Soochow and Changchow White Rice Improves by Five Fen

(Shanghai South) Yesterday, more than thirty sources from various gangs (4,500-6,600 shih) arrived, and wholesale sales at the beginning of the market still seemed normal. Later, the weather suddenly turned cloudy, and buyers' sentiment tightened, causing the situation to move upward. Local shops actively purchased, about 3,000+ shih. Prices for Soochow and Changchow gangs' rice improved by five fen. As for the purchases by out-of-town buyers, only those from Beiyang, Tianjin, and Yantai showed activity, resulting in the purchase of more than 2,000 bags. Although sellers took the opportunity to push up prices for late rice, buyers were reluctant to loosen their grip, so the slightly increased prices for Qingjiao, Songjiang, Sixian, and Xilian late rice remained in a tight situation. Although Du Yang pointed rice was affected by the out-of-town pointed rice, market sentiment remained somewhat firm, allowing it to hold steady. Prices for Yinbianyuan followed the variable market conditions, with little change.

(Shanghai North) Yesterday, thirteen or fourteen boats from various gangs arrived from the river region. Sales of various goods in the market showed slight improvement. High-quality white rice remained stable, while medium and lower grades increased slightly. Sheep Du pointed rice remained firm, and out-of-town buyer's pointed rice, early thin rice, and Yinbianyuan rice were firm.

客秈本銷活潑

Customer Indica Rice Sales Active

Yesterday, the market for customer indica rice saw active buying by local buyers. Although merchants continued to seek to sell, the market was no longer as sluggish as the previous day. After opening flat in the morning, the market picked up as local sales were brisk. Later, orders came from Fuzhou, Shantou, Wenzhou and other gangs, and the market immediately rebounded. As a result, prices of higher quality goods rose by two or three fen, while medium and lower grades remained unchanged. A total of 4,467 bags were sold, including 100 bags of machine-milled rice to Wenzhou, 297 bags of Baijing rice to Shantou, and more than 850 bags to Fuzhou, with the remainder being purchased by local buyers. Because local demand remains strong, the market can temporarily stand firm.

Soybean Sales Gradually Decline

Yesterday, soybean sales weakened and the market trended downward. In general, the abundant supply and sluggish sales made it difficult for the market to develop. Although factories were active, soybean demand also decreased due to the poor price of soybean cake. Yesterday, one cart of Linzhun Guandou beans was sold for $2.35, and one cart of Huaiyuan beans was sold for $2.40. Retail sales in the local market totaled about four carts, including two carts of Zhengyang Guandou beans at $2.68 to $2.65, one cart of Yingzhou beans at $2.57 to $2.56, and one cart of Bozhou beans at $2.52.

糖市　潮青糖市勢轉定

Sugar Market: Chaoqing Sugar Market Trend Stabilizes

Yesterday, the sugar market's actual sales remained sluggish, and the guild's sentiment remained cautious. Prices for coarse sugar like 24 were listed at $19.70, with only dozens of bags traded. The A grade of Hainan brown sugar and Yantai gang sugar saw some movement, with a total of five or six hundred bags sold at prices of $13.30, $13.40, and $13.50. Due to abundant inventories, the market remained stable. A batch of Chaoqing sugar arrived yesterday on the Yih Ho Company's He Sheng ship, totaling 3,357 bags. Sales have been slightly slow in recent days, and the situation has stabilized.

南北貨　黑胡椒地價報漲

North-South Goods: Black Pepper Landed Price Reported Higher

Arrivals of pepper are not many, while sales in Shanghai are flat. The current price for grade one is $45.50, and for black large pepper it is $45. However, the landed price has increased, with Shanghai asking for $47, creating an inverted situation.

Although supplies of fennel are scarce, sales are difficult to improve, as yesterday's special report indicated. The current market price for Nanning goods is over $24.70, with wholesale sales at $25. Beihai goods are selling for only $23.50, and the market is stable.

油市白桐油漢市後轉機

Oil Market: White Tung Oil Sees a Turnaround After Hankow

The trading of white tung oil in Hankow with foreign firms has been scarce in recent days, leading to successive declines. After opening at $24.50, the price fell to $24, then to $23.70, and then to $23.30 or $23.40. It was rumored that the market price on the previous day was $23. Judging from the situation, foreign firms are not making large purchases, with each transaction involving only dozens of tons, while the supply continues uninterrupted, making the market's weakness inevitable. Unexpectedly, it was suddenly rumored the night before last that foreign firms in Hankow had raised the price to $24, according to reports from those who had received telegrams from Hankow. The matter was indeed true, and foreign firms in Hankow must have made a large purchase. Foreign firms often purchase goods repeatedly, and it is impossible for outsiders to grasp their movements. Therefore, large purchases often come suddenly, and the changes in market conditions can vary greatly. This makes foreign trade difficult to deal with, and even those experienced in this field often miss opportunities. However, foreign firms have established branches in the production areas of Sichuan and Hunan to collect and handle goods. Therefore, although Hankow is nominally the center, it is gradually losing its ability to lead the market. The rise and fall of the market are controlled by foreign firms. If prices rise to $25 or above, foreign firms will stop buying, and the market will inevitably trend downward. This is why domestic sales have lost their ability to influence the market, and this has been the case for some time. Therefore, even if foreign sales prices can rise to $25 or above, it is difficult for them to be sustained, and this has been seen frequently. If this increase can be sustained, it will probably only reach $25, which would be the limit. Foreign firms will undoubtedly use their usual tactic of stopping purchases to counter the upward trend. Although local firms in Shanghai rely on Hankow, they mainly import Zhejiang tung oil. Although the Hankow market has recently seen sudden fluctuations, Zhejiang tung oil has not followed suit. This is probably because spring sales are not yet strong, so both buying and selling are very calm.

五金　英白鐵售價步鬆

Hardware: British Galvanized Iron Sheet Prices Gradually Ease

The trading of British galvanized iron sheets has not seen much progress recently, as the market is flooded with goods from the Orient, which has greatly affected sales. The current price for 3x7 foot sheets is estimated at $1.20 each, down another five fen from before. 3x6 foot sheets are priced at $1, also down three or four fen from the previous level. Thick galvanized iron sheets are selling for $12.20 for 24 gauge, $13.10 for 26 gauge, and $13.80 for 28 gauge, all up one or two jiao from before, but there is still no major progress in future trading, so people in the industry are quite pessimistic.

18-gauge cigarette tinplate suddenly reported a shortage yesterday, with the standard price rising by one jiao, estimated at $8.80 per picul. It is said that trading is still active.
