Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

After Reading "An Open Letter to College Students"

— Meng Ruo

Mr. Pan Guangdan recently published "An Open Letter to College Students" in the latest issue of "Hua Nian". Mr. Pan's letter is intended for college students to read. Although I am not currently a college student, I am very happy to read it, and after reading it, I want to say a few words. This should be my right, right? The intention of Mr. Pan's open letter is undoubtedly very sincere. He sees that current college students are not only delayed by corrupt university education but are also often used by political activists, resulting in the loss of everything. Therefore, he specifically puts forward two methods to offer to them, hoping to remedy the future of college students. How should we thank him!

What are the two points that Mr. Pan wants to discuss publicly? (1) Instrumental knowledge. (2) A detached interest in current affairs. Regarding the first point, Mr. Pan advocates: "Whether your interest is in science or liberal arts, I believe that you should at least master Chinese and English fluently. You should not only be able to read Chinese quickly but also be able to write fluently. You should be able to understand the essence of a piece of writing in English without flipping through a dictionary." At first glance, these words seem to belittle college students too much. Why should a college student still do this kind of work? In fact, he is not wrong. Under today's Chinese university education, not to mention that advanced knowledge cannot be obtained, but even the ability to read and write Chinese and English freely is probably not the majority, right? It is heartbreaking to say this, but the fact is like this, so how can we conceal it? Therefore, I think that Mr. Pan's instructions are really a most pertinent attempt. A college student who can achieve this level, as Mr. Pan said, will not only benefit a lot in academic progress but will also find it easier to work in society.

As for the second point, I feel that this is truly Mr. Pan's painstaking words. He reminds a group of college students to cultivate a detached interest in the current political situation. He believes that the environment we are currently in is a world that emphasizes ideologies. A college student, if he does not have a detached interest, will sooner or later join their ranks. This will certainly increase their strength, but it will be a great loss to oneself. Therefore, he advocates, "Your personal political activities should be postponed until after graduation. Before graduating, your interest in politics should be completely detached, like your interest in other knowledge and things, and not be dominated by private interests." Mr. Cai Yuanpei tells us, "Study without forgetting to save the country, save the country without forgetting to study." Our country has now been brought to such a terrible state, and all Chinese people should do their part to contribute to the country. Moreover, students are the backbone of society, so how can we stand idly by and bury ourselves in books? Therefore, I believe that a college student engaging in the national salvation movement is worthy of encouragement. However, it is permissible to sacrifice oneself for the country voluntarily, but one should oppose being used for the activities of individuals or factions. Mr. Pan said it very clearly, "I believe that teaching a person whose thinking is immature and whose knowledge is insufficient to join a party is not only unhelpful to that individual but also hinders the organization of a party." How incisive these words are. I feel that in the current state, this point is more important than instrumental knowledge.

The above is a little thought I had after reading Mr. Pan's letter. Finally, Mr. Pan's conclusion is this: "Achieving the second point can settle your mind for studying, and achieving the first point can further enrich your ability to study. With both mind and ability in place, you will not fail the generous opportunities given to you by the country, society, and family."

Page 22

The Art of Sleeping (Part Two) Yi Lu

—

The physiologist has never opened his eyes so wide before. He stares blankly at the ceiling, slowly reaches into his pocket, and pulls out a box of "Maistre" cigarettes. The lid is open, but there's only a half-smoked cigarette butt left inside. I know there's nothing for me, so I continue:

"In the morning, the clock strikes ten. The bed shakes again. The man wakes up, sticks his head out, and looks at the clock, 'Oh! Ten o'clock!' The woman also seems to wake up and says quickly, 'What's the rush? Come on, sleep for another moment.' 'There are things to do at the company.' 'Oh my! Are you the general manager?' The woman's hand reaches over, and finally, the man's head also falls back down... Friends, think about it, if this isn't art, what is it?"

The physiologist is a bit excited. He's still holding the half-inch-long cigarette butt in his hand. But he's very clever; he understands that this is bourgeois. Suddenly, he throws the cigarette butt away, looking very indignant but also very disappointed. Finally, he blurts out this reluctant remark: "This is art? Art is for everyone."

"Everyone? Well, this is just one example I'm giving. Are commoners like us worthy of experiencing this magnificent art? Don't even think about it, don't even think about it, don't even think about it. However, we have our own comforts in sleeping. Since we can't get jobs as clerks or bookkeepers, and we don't have the fate to be anything like bank tellers or bureau members, our sleeping has to be free and unrestrained. We can sleep as late as we want and get up as late as we want. Although the room we sleep in is simple—the walls are plastered with newspapers, the table has only three legs left, with a stick replacing the broken one, two or three broken benches, the bed is two long benches with a door placed on top, covered with three or four inches of straw, a quilt with seven holes and eight tears, and a black, damp, tattered cotton blanket—when it comes time for us to sleep, we can still tuck our legs into the cotton blanket and lean our upper bodies against the wall; we can still read last night's big evening newspaper while lying down. If it happens to be a rainy day, then there's even more natural and melodious music for us to listen to and enjoy. The "chala-la" sound of water leaking from the broken drainpipe to the ground, the "dada" sound of rain hitting the newspaper-covered window, plus the "puff-puff" sound of the paper getting damp and being blown by the wind—these are all enough for us to enjoy. If you want to hear a little tune, you might as well ask your little bound-footed wife to sing a song... 'In the first month...sleeping... celebrating the Lantern Festival... I see... my sister is born pretty...' And if there's no rice to cook tomorrow, then get angry and cover your head to sleep through the day. 'Rejoicing even in a dry rut,' 'Isn't that a gentleman?' Isn't this an art of 'nothingness'? Why isn't it for everyone?"

The physiologist is somewhat excited again, as if because I brought up his wife. A slight smile appears on his face, but in an instant, it disappears again. Then, he sighs without saying a word. After all, he has been seduced by materialism and must be thinking: Shame, shame!

"However, things in the world can't be absolute; there always has to be an exception. Just as sleeping can be called art, it's the same. The sleeping of the portly and prosperous is certainly art; the sleeping of friends who are poor and have no way out is even more art. But those people who hold their rice bowls and tremble, serving someone else's meal, can't appreciate the comfort of sleeping; their sleeping can't be considered art. Friends, you have to understand: the comfort of sleeping is appreciated when you're already sleepy but haven't fallen asleep yet, and when you're already awake but haven't gotten up yet. When they sleep, they collapse as soon as they lie down, and they fall asleep as soon as they collapse; when dawn comes, they wake up and get up immediately. What art is there to speak of? If they also start talking about art, their rice bowls will definitely be irreconcilable with them, leading to a business shutdown. So we are still happy. Although no one pities us, no one interferes with us or controls us. How unhappy would that make us? We can also appreciate the comfort of sleeping to our heart's content!"

The physiologist's face is expressionless. At this time, I am truly stirred up with a belly full of worries and feel somewhat "sentimental". I pace back and forth along the edge of the bed a few times, and suddenly, I see a glimmer of light. This light gets bigger and bigger, brighter and brighter, and finally illuminates me, causing me to shout out involuntarily: "Why not walk on the great path of life but insist on crawling through this dog hole? Isn't that foolish? Tomorrow, I'll pick out a bundle of old books from under the bed and send them to the used bookstore in Chenghuang Temple to exchange for a dollar. Then I'll go to the entrance of Xinbeimen to buy an aviation lottery ticket, and if I win 50,000 yuan, wouldn't I instantly become a Buddha?" Unexpectedly, the physiologist rises and responds, saying: "Excellent words! This old man should rise and imitate them!" (End)

The Story of a Homeless Child (Part Four)

— Made by Chen Jingsheng

Listen! A knock at the door, it turns out to be a war horse.

Spring, Is It Worth Praising?

— Xiao Zhi

丨Reminiscing About the Departed Winter丨

Spring, always praised and admired by people, has indeed returned to the world. Nature has taken on a completely new and vibrant atmosphere. Many people, those who naturally praise it, have also genuinely changed to a warm and smiling countenance, their mouths constantly shouting, "Welcome spring and receive blessings!"

However, spring, I detest it the most, resent it, curse it. Of all the seasons, spring leaves the worst impression on me! Because it has never brought me any "blessings." What it brings me is only annoying, depressing, cursed warmth! This warmth has made me suffer from many illnesses, and it even triggers my old ailments. My active and forward-moving spirit is all tricked away by its bewitchment, and I become a soft, sentimental, and decadent person!

How cursed this season should be! Its warmth has deceived me, and it has deceived many others who share my fate. It has numbed me, and it has numbed many others who share my fate! Yet, people, pitiful insects of people, still foolishly wait for its "blessings," waiting for joy to descend. Isn't this too contrary to reason?

Perhaps when spring arrives in the world, it causes the withered old trees to sprout tender buds, and the withered yellow grass to grow green shoots, giving the world another painting of red and green colors, and all things undergo a revival. However, the spring feelings that spring brings to people are forever melancholic, lazy, depressed, and haggard, stealing away people's vitality and vigor like a hypnotist. When people arrive, when people arrive in spring, they lose the power of life. This is the exact opposite of how grass and trees gain the opportunity for revival in spring.

In this way, the world of things and the world of people are forever irreconcilable. Spring, envied by so many, only ever gives people melancholy, numbness, and a lazy inability to live. This signifies the decline of people and the prosperity of things. Many heartbroken poets of the past searched for spring feelings in the world of things, but never have they seen a single infatuated poet utter a sound of joy in the world of people. Poets in the world of people can never find spring feelings; what they find are some "emptiness, like a dream," such desolate sighs.

The meaning of spring is to give people melancholy, numbness, pointless sentimentality, and decadence. This makes me infinitely nostalgic for the recently departed winter and pay it the greatest respect! Because winter, the severe and great winter, although it exerts its supreme power over people, causing many to succumb and even sacrifice themselves under its stern might, it is precisely because of this immense and supreme pressure that it keenly stimulates people's nerves, giving people a powerful warning: "Defend! Defend against this cruel and harsh winter!" Think about it, when a person is hungry, unless they are a fool or a weakling, will they just wait to starve to death? Similarly, when it's cold, they will naturally develop a great courage and vitality to survive! Look again, in this season, the roaring of the wind, the clamor of the trees, the hard and brittle ice, the piercingly cold snow, the bone-chilling cold, stiffness, bleeding... Isn't this enough tension and vigilance? Struggle, uplift, inspire, and strive become the active, forward-moving, and inevitable force of reaction in this season!

Winter tightly compels people to grasp the power of life, risking the full fire of life, to be active in a human world purified by pure snow. How majestic, how great! Whoever has power, whoever has life. How vivid, how brave, and how full of righteous spirit!

Spring, although it also has its flames, these flames can only burn people's lives, cause sorrow, ignite the courage to tend towards a decadent body, and lull people into a dream... Spring, creating so many "human sins," is spring still worth our praise?

We cannot forget the stimulation that winter gives us, the great vitality of life. Vigilant people, holding the solemnity of winter, bravely engage in battle with the spirit of open warfare! However, under the anesthesia of spring, we still need to muster the spirit of battle!

Amateur Mailbox

I Don't Want Her Anymore

Editor Sir,

I am twenty years old now. When I was seventeen, by the order of my parents and the words of a matchmaker, I got engaged to a woman from the village in front of our village. According to our local customs, women mostly go outside to work in factories. So this woman also worked in a nearby factory. Last year, the factory closed down due to losses, and the other party faced financial difficulties. The whole family moved to Shanghai to make a living. After arriving in Shanghai, a place where all evils are committed, this woman soon became romantically involved with someone else. This is news that was spread by others, with no definite evidence; later, my family suddenly received a letter from Shanghai with no sender, the content of which said, "This woman is not keeping to proper feminine behavior outside, recklessly flirting and messing around with people. I am calling your mother to come to Shanghai to take her back" and other such things. My mother ignored it and let her go. Of course, when I received this news, I wanted to dissolve the engagement and not have her anymore. However, I don't have a proper way to do it. Now, I have written down several questions below. Please teach me, sir:

(1) If I publish a declaration in the newspaper to dissolve the engagement, will it be legally effective?

(2) Can the anonymous letter be used as evidence? Will it be legally effective?

(3) Can the betrothal gifts from before be recovered?

With best regards,

Respectfully, Zhang Mengjiong

Editor's Note: Mr. Zhang's inquiries are answered separately as follows:

(1) An engagement must be dissolved by suing the court; it cannot be resolved with a "declaration in the newspaper."

(2) An anonymous letter cannot be used as evidence.

(3) If an engagement is invalid, the party at fault should be responsible for restoring the innocent party to their original state. Therefore, if the fault lies with the other party, Mr. Zhang can, of course, demand the return of the betrothal gifts from her.

In short, Mr. Zhang still cannot be sure if his fiancée is committing adultery with someone else, so it seems there is no legal basis for dissolving the engagement. However, since this engagement was not made by Mr. Zhang himself, there is no harm in denying it, but this should be considered and decided by Mr. Zhang himself. The editor cannot strongly advise Mr. Zhang to proceed with dissolving the engagement.

Substitute Mail: Xu Zhengshou, please note: I am sorry that I could not reply immediately about the matter you entrusted me with because I was busy.

Self-Professional Introduction

Miss Hao, from Shanghai, 17 years old, graduated from the senior group of a municipal primary school, and worked in a certain hospital. Now she is willing to take on a comparable occupation, monthly salary is negotiable. Mailing address: No. 8 Ruyi Lane, Jinjiafang, inside the city.

Ms. Chen, 18 years old, high school education, served in a store for half a year, if there is a suitable occupation, the salary is negotiable, mailing address is No. 79 Huayuanfang, Route du Père Froc, French Concession.

Ms. Mou, from Jiangsu, 25 years old, with a university degree, served as a junior high school teacher, as well as a senior and junior primary school headteacher. She has some experience in teaching and now wishes to take on the above occupation, or as a home tutor. The monthly salary is thirty yuan. A shop guarantor is available. Mailing address: Yushouyan, c/o Zhengfeng Middle School, Route Haig.

Yujun, from Jiangsu, 39 years old, graduated from the Department of Commerce, and studied medicine in a church hospital for three years. He served as an outport representative of a certain Shanghai foreign firm and a certain pharmacy and a certain pharmaceutical company for more than ten years. He is familiar with the pharmaceutical companies and hospitals accessible by train, car, and ship throughout the country, and also has connections in the military medical community. Now, he intends to serve as an outport representative in the Western medicine industry. Salary is negotiable. Those wishing to hire him, please send a letter to No. 443 Zhejiang Road.

Fiction

Lulu's Victory (7)

— Written by Italian M. Serrao, Translated by Jingxin

"Robert sat in the car and passed by here, he was wearing a gray coat."

"Good heavens! How do you know all this? I thought you were reading!"

"I was just sitting by the window."

"You recognized him even when you didn't look at Robert? Strange! Did he bow to you?"

"Yes."

"How did he take off his hat?"

"Oh! Just like he usually does."

"Did you return the greeting?"

"Do you think I understand etiquette?"

"At least you smiled at him, right?"

"No! That's... I don't know."

"You are bland, Sophia. Robert told me about you last night."

"He told you I was bland?"

"No, but he asked me why your personality is so cold and so different from mine. So I recited a long eulogy to him; I told him you are better, gentler, and more lovely than me, your only shortcoming is that you hide all these good qualities. Think about it, you listened to my speech with great interest; finally, he asked me why I hate him—"

"Hate him?"

"That's what he said, you have to know, his words are not completely wrong; you treat him too unkindly. But even on this point, I defended you; I told a little lie, I told him that you really like him very much, and that you praise him extremely highly—"

"Lulu!"

"I know this isn't true, but Robert likes you very much, and isn't it too heartless of you to treat him like a stranger?"

Sophia opened her arms and hugged her sister's neck, kissing her; Lulu endured it for a while, and said softly in a lovely voice:

"Why don't you like Robert a little?"

The sister suddenly stopped for a moment, did not say a word, and backed away.
